  // Restore the saved color scheme preference, or
  // enact the browser preference if "automatic", 
  // without expecting DOM load to have completed.
  //
  // Also restore any saved readingmode and ToC display preferences.
  function initializeReadingPreferences() {
    let saved_theme = localStorage.getItem("ar5iv_theme") || "automatic";
    if (saved_theme === "automatic") {
      if (window.matchMedia("(prefers-color-scheme: dark)").matches) {
        saved_theme = "dark";
      }
    }
    if (saved_theme == "dark") {
      document.documentElement.setAttribute("data-theme", "dark");
    } else {
      document.documentElement.setAttribute("data-theme", "light");
    }

    const tocDisplay = localStorage.getItem('arxiv_html_paper_toc_display');
    if (tocDisplay) {
      document.documentElement.setAttribute("data-toc-display", tocDisplay);
    }
    const readingMode = localStorage.getItem('arxiv_html_paper_reading_mode');
    if (readingMode) {
      document.documentElement.setAttribute("data-reading-mode", readingMode);
    }
  }
  // Run as soon as JS starts, to minimize repainting
  initializeReadingPreferences();
</script>

<div id="abstract1" class="ltx_abstract">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_title_abstract">Abstract</h6>
<p class="ltx_p">Photonic quantum processors naturally produce intrinsically stochastic measurement outcomes, offering a hardware-native source of structured randomness that can be exploited during machine-learning training. Here we introduce Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation (PQKD), a hybrid quantum photonic–classical framework in which a programmable photonic circuit generates a compact conditioning signal that constrains and guides a parameter-efficient student network during distillation from a high-capacity teacher. PQKD replaces fully trainable convolutional kernels with dictionary convolutions: each layer learns only a small set of shared spatial basis filters, while sample-dependent channel-mixing weights are derived from shot-limited photonic features and mapped through a fixed linear transform. Training alternates between standard gradient-based optimisation of the student and sampling-robust, gradient-free updates of photonic parameters, avoiding differentiation through photonic hardware. Across MNIST, Fashion-MNIST and CIFAR-10, PQKD traces a controllable compression–accuracy frontier, remaining close to teacher performance on simpler benchmarks under aggressive convolutional compression. Performance degrades predictably with finite sampling, consistent with shot-noise scaling, and exponential moving-average feature smoothing suppresses high-frequency shot-noise fluctuations, extending the practical operating regime at moderate shot budgets.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_classification">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_title_classification">keywords: </h6>Photonic quantum computing, Hybrid quantum–classical machine learning, Parameter generation, Model compression
</div>
<section id="S1" class="ltx_section">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">1 </span>Introduction</h2>

<div id="S1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.p1.1" class="ltx_p">As the realm of computing continues to evolve, the integration of optical technologies has emerged as a decisive frontier for processing and information transfer<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">mcmahon2023physics</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">solli2015analog</span>]</cite>. Traditional electronic computing faces increasing constraints in speed, bandwidth, and energy efficiency as data demands accelerate in an increasingly connected world<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">waldrop2016chips</span>]</cite>. Optical computing, which exploits the physics of light for high-bandwidth transport and parallelizable transformations, offers an alternative path toward ultra-fast data movement and potentially more energy-efficient computation<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">xue2022nanosecond</span>]</cite>. Recent advances in photonic devices—including low-loss waveguides<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">bose2024anneal</span>]</cite>, stable on-chip lasers<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">xiang2021high</span>]</cite>, high-speed modulators<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">wang2018integrated</span>]</cite>, and scalable integrated photonic circuits<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">shekhar2024roadmapping</span>]</cite>—make this an especially timely moment to explore unconventional optical computing architectures that go beyond incremental improvements to electronic logic<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">hua2025integrated</span>]</cite>.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.p2.1" class="ltx_p">Within this broader landscape, photonic quantum computing provides a distinctive set of computational primitives rooted in quantum interference and measurement<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">yu2025QTDA</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">psiquantum2025manufacturable</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">yu2023GBS</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">wang2020integrated</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">bromley2020applications</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">zhong2020quantum</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">o2009photonic</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">knill2001scheme</span>]</cite>.
Of particular relevance to near-term implementations is the continuous-variable (CV) paradigm, where information is encoded in field quadratures and manipulated using Gaussian operations (such as squeezing, phase shifts, and interferometry), optionally augmented by non-Gaussian resources and measurements<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">weedbrook2012gaussian</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">braunstein2005quantum</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">lloyd1999quantum</span>]</cite>.
CV photonic platforms are naturally aligned with integrated optics<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">stokowski2023integrated</span>]</cite> and can operate at high repetition rates<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">asavanant2021time</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">asavanant2019generation</span>]</cite>, making them compelling candidates for hardware-in-the-loop learning and optimization<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">cimini2024variational</span>]</cite>.
Recent community efforts have also begun to establish reproducible baselines for photonic quantum machine learning under hardware-feasible constraints<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">notton2025photonic_baselines</span>]</cite>, complementing broader perspectives on optical routes to quantum neural networks<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">yu2024shedding_light</span>]</cite>.
At the same time, the shot-limited nature of photonic measurements and the practical constraints of near-term devices motivate algorithmic designs that can extract utility from stochastic measurement statistics without requiring fault tolerance or full end-to-end differentiability<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">preskill2018quantum</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">scriva2024challenges</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">katabarwa2024early</span>]</cite>.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.p3.1" class="ltx_p">In parallel, machine learning models—particularly convolutional neural networks—have achieved remarkable performance, yet their growing parameter counts hinder deployment in resource-constrained settings<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">lecun2015deep</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">cheng2018model</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">howard2017mobilenets</span>]</cite>.
Model compression has therefore become central to practical AI, and knowledge distillation is among the most effective strategies: a compact student model learns not only from labelled data but also from a high-capacity teacher’s predictive behaviour<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">cheng2018model</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">hinton2015distilling</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">romero2015experimental</span>]</cite>.
Beyond classical KD, quantum-enhanced conditioning signals and kernelized relations have recently been explored as training-time resources while preserving fully classical deployment<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">liu2025qrkd</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">chen2025qsvm_validation</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">chen2024stellar_qsvm</span>]</cite>.
However, aggressively shrinking a student often degrades performance, especially when compression targets the early convolutional layers that shape representation quality<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">zeiler2014visualizing</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">vadera2022methods</span>]</cite>.
This tension suggests an opportunity for new compression mechanisms that retain expressivity while drastically reducing the number of trainable degrees of freedom, particularly when the additional structure is used only during training.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.p4.1" class="ltx_p">Here we propose Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation (PQKD), a hybrid quantum-photonic–classical framework that links photonic CV hardware with parameter-efficient distillation.
The design is inspired by a line of training-time-only quantum-assisted parameter-efficient learning approaches (e.g., Quantum-Train and its variants), which leverage quantum models to generate or modulate classical parameters during training while keeping inference purely classical<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">lin2024qtlstm_flood</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">liu2024qtrl</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">lin2024qtcnn_deepfake</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">liu2024qt_tn_mapping</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">chen2024distqtrl</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">liu2025qpa_typhoon</span>]</cite>.
PQKD uses a CV photonic quantum circuit as a compact, trainable generator of structured stochastic signals that condition a parameter-efficient student network during distillation.
Rather than learning full convolutional kernels, the student represents each convolutional layer using a low-dimensional basis, while a photonic feature vector—computed from shot-limited measurement statistics of a 16-mode circuit—controls how those bases mix across channels.
Training alternates between (i) updating the student with standard distillation objectives to match the teacher and (ii) updating the photonic circuit parameters with sampling-robust, gradient-free optimization compatible with finite-shot measurements and black-box hardware access.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.p5.1" class="ltx_p">We validate PQKD on MNIST as a controlled benchmark where compression–accuracy trade-offs can be quantified precisely and where the effects of sampling noise can be studied without confounding factors. In this setting, PQKD maintains strong classification performance while enabling substantially stronger compression than conventional students, particularly when compression is applied across the full convolutional stack. The approach exposes clear, experimentally meaningful knobs—such as the basis rank used to parameterize convolutional filters and the photonic parameter budget—that directly determine the achievable compression–accuracy frontier.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.p6.1" class="ltx_p">More broadly, PQKD illustrates how integrated photonic platforms—especially CV architectures—can contribute to practical learning workflows not only as accelerators for linear optical transforms, but as hardware-aligned generators of rich measurement statistics that can be harnessed to reduce model complexity in AI systems. By bridging photonic quantum hardware constraints with mainstream distillation pipelines, PQKD provides a blueprint for future studies on larger datasets, more expressive optical circuits, and rigorous comparisons against classical conditioning and hypernetwork baselines under matched parameter budgets.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S2" class="ltx_section">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">2 </span>Results</h2>

<figure id="S2.F1" class="ltx_figure"><img src="2603.14898v1/x1.png" id="S2.F1.g1" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_landscape" width="830" height="554" alt="Refer to caption">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 1: </span><span id="S2.F1.26.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Hardware–algorithm co-design for PQKD enabling neural network compression.</span>
A CV photonic module prepares a fixed input state <math id="S2.F1.13.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\rho_{\mathrm{in}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rho_{\mathrm{in}}</annotation></semantics></math> and applies a programmable unitary <math id="S2.F1.14.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="U(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>U</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">U(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> implemented by an integrated interferometric mesh. The output state <math id="S2.F1.15.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\rho_{\theta}=U(\theta)\rho_{\mathrm{in}}U^{\dagger}(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>U</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mi>U</mi><mo>†</mo></msup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rho_{\theta}=U(\theta)\rho_{\mathrm{in}}U^{\dagger}(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> is measured using an SNSPD array with time-tagging, producing i.i.d. samples <math id="S2.F1.16.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\{\omega_{s}\}_{s=1}^{S}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msubsup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><msub><mi>ω</mi><mi>s</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>S</mi></msubsup><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{\omega_{s}\}_{s=1}^{S}</annotation></semantics></math> and an empirical distribution <math id="S2.F1.17.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\hat{p}_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\hat{p}_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math>. A robust classical feature extractor <math id="S2.F1.18.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Phi(\cdot)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">⋅</mo><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Phi(\cdot)</annotation></semantics></math> maps <math id="S2.F1.19.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\hat{p}_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\hat{p}_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math> to a fixed-length conditioning vector <math id="S2.F1.20.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)=\Phi(\hat{p}_{\theta})\in\mathbb{R}^{d}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mi>d</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)=\Phi(\hat{p}_{\theta})\in\mathbb{R}^{d}</annotation></semantics></math>, which modulates the student model <math id="S2.F1.21.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f_{S}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>f</mi><mi>S</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">f_{S}</annotation></semantics></math> during knowledge distillation from a pretrained teacher <math id="S2.F1.22.m10" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f_{T}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>f</mi><mi>T</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">f_{T}</annotation></semantics></math>. Crucially, <math id="S2.F1.23.m11" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> is updated by a classical optimiser using a distillation objective <math id="S2.F1.24.m12" class="ltx_Math" alttext="L_{\mathrm{KD}}(\omega,\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>L</mi><mi>KD</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ω</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">L_{\mathrm{KD}}(\omega,\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> and requires sampling only, avoiding differentiation through photonic hardware.</figcaption>
</figure>
<section id="S2.SS1" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">2.1 </span>Photonic quantum-enhanced knowledge distillation as a structured compression mechanism</h3>

<section id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Teacher–student distillation objective.</h5>

<div id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1.7" class="ltx_p">Let <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathcal{D}=\{(x_{n},y_{n})\}_{n=1}^{N}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">𝒟</mi><mo>=</mo><msubsup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>N</mi></msubsup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathcal{D}=\{(x_{n},y_{n})\}_{n=1}^{N}</annotation></semantics></math> denote the training set with <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y_{n}\in\{1,\dots,C\}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>y</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>C</mi><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">y_{n}\in\{1,\dots,C\}</annotation></semantics></math>. A trained teacher network produces logits <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="t(x)\in\mathbb{R}^{C}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>t</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mi>C</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">t(x)\in\mathbb{R}^{C}</annotation></semantics></math> and the student produces logits <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="s(x;w,\theta)\in\mathbb{R}^{C}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo>;</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mi>C</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">s(x;w,\theta)\in\mathbb{R}^{C}</annotation></semantics></math>, where <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> denotes trainable <em id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1.7.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">classical</em> parameters in the student and <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1.6.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> denotes <em id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1.7.2" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">photonic circuit</em> parameters. For temperature <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p1.7.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau&gt;0" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\tau&gt;0</annotation></semantics></math>, define softened distributions</p>

</div>
<div id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p2.2" class="ltx_p">We train the student using a standard distillation objective combining hard-label supervision and teacher matching [See Supplementary Information]:</p>
<table id="S2.E2" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>

stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>∼</mo><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">𝒟</mi></mrow></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.600em" minsize="1.600em">[</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>λ</mi><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mpadded style="width:1.412em;" width="1.412em"><mi>CE</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><mi>y</mi><mo rspace="0.337em">,</mo><mrow><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>S</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo>;</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>λ</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mi>τ</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mpadded style="width:1.431em;" width="1.431em"><mi>KL</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><mrow><mrow><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>T</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo rspace="0.170em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="0.448em">∥</mo><mrow><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>S</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo>;</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo maxsize="1.600em" minsize="1.600em">]</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathcal{L}_{\mathrm{KD}}(w,\theta)=\mathbb{E}_{(x,y)\sim\mathcal{D}}\Big[\lambda\,\mathrm{CE}\!\left(y,\,p_{S}^{(1)}(x;w,\theta)\right)+(1-\lambda)\,\tau^{2}\,\mathrm{KL}\!\left(p_{T}^{(\tau)}(x)\,\|\,p_{S}^{(\tau)}(x;w,\theta)\right)\Big],</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(2)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p2.1" class="ltx_p">with <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\lambda\in[0,1]" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>λ</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\lambda\in[0,1]</annotation></semantics></math>. The KL term is equivalent (up to an additive constant independent of student parameters) to cross-entropy against teacher soft targets:</p>
<table id="S2.E3" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathrm{KL}\!\left(p_{T}^{(\tau)}\|p_{S}^{(\tau)}\right)=\mathrm{CE}\!\left(p_{T}^{(\tau)},p_{S}^{(\tau)}\right)-\mathrm{H}\!\left(p_{T}^{(\tau)}\right)," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mpadded style="width:1.431em;" width="1.431em"><mi>KL</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><mrow><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>T</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo>∥</mo><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>S</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup></mrow><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mpadded style="width:1.412em;" width="1.412em"><mi>CE</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>T</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo>,</mo><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>S</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mpadded style="width:0.742em;" width="0.742em"><mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>T</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{KL}\!\left(p_{T}^{(\tau)}\|p_{S}^{(\tau)}\right)=\mathrm{CE}\!\left(p_{T}^{(\tau)},p_{S}^{(\tau)}\right)-\mathrm{H}\!\left(p_{T}^{(\tau)}\right),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(3)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p2.3" class="ltx_p">thereby transferring the teacher’s <em id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px1.p2.3.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">relative class structure</em> to the student. This is particularly important under aggressive compression, where hard-label training alone can be insufficient to identify a well-generalising solution within a restricted hypothesis class.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Continuous-variable photonic quantum feature map.</h5>

<div id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p1.3" class="ltx_p">PQKD couples distillation to a photonic module that produces a compact, distributional conditioning signal. Let <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\rho_{\mathrm{in}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rho_{\mathrm{in}}</annotation></semantics></math> be a fixed input state over <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>N</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N</annotation></semantics></math> photonic modes and let <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="U(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>U</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">U(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> be a parameterised CV unitary realised by an integrated photonic circuit (e.g., interferometric networks with phase shifts). The circuit output state is</p>
<table id="S2.E4" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\rho_{\theta}=U(\theta)\,\rho_{\mathrm{in}}\,U(\theta)^{\dagger}." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>U</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>U</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>†</mo></msup></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rho_{\theta}=U(\theta)\,\rho_{\mathrm{in}}\,U(\theta)^{\dagger}.</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(4)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.3" class="ltx_p">Let <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Omega" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi mathvariant="normal">Ω</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Omega</annotation></semantics></math> denote the (finite or countable) set of classical measurement outcomes and let
<math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\{M_{\omega}\}_{\omega\in\Omega}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>ω</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mrow><mi>ω</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">Ω</mi></mrow></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{M_{\omega}\}_{\omega\in\Omega}</annotation></semantics></math> be a POVM on the <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>N</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N</annotation></semantics></math>-mode Hilbert space (covering projective measurements as a special case,
as well as realistic detectors such as photon-number-resolving or threshold detection). This induces the output distribution</p>
<table id="S2.E5" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{\theta}(\omega)=\mathrm{Tr}\!\left(M_{\omega}\,\rho_{\theta}\right),\qquad\omega\in\Omega,\qquad\sum_{\omega\in\Omega}p_{\theta}(\omega)=1." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ω</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mpadded style="width:1.032em;" width="1.032em"><mi>Tr</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>ω</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub></mrow><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="2.167em">,</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>ω</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">Ω</mi></mrow><mo rspace="2.000em">,</mo><mrow><mrow><munder><mo movablelimits="false">∑</mo><mrow><mi>ω</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">Ω</mi></mrow></munder><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ω</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">p_{\theta}(\omega)=\mathrm{Tr}\!\left(M_{\omega}\,\rho_{\theta}\right),\qquad\omega\in\Omega,\qquad\sum_{\omega\in\Omega}p_{\theta}(\omega)=1.</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(5)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.6" class="ltx_p">With <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> shots, we obtain i.i.d. outcomes <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.5.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\omega_{1},\ldots,\omega_{S}\sim p_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>ω</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>ω</mi><mi>S</mi></msub></mrow><mo>∼</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\omega_{1},\ldots,\omega_{S}\sim p_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math> and an empirical distribution <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.6.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{p}_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{p}_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math>.
The photonic feature is a deterministic, fixed-length summary</p>
<table id="S2.E6" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E6.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)=\Phi(\widehat{p}_{\theta})\in\mathbb{R}^{d}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mi>d</mi></msup></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)=\Phi(\widehat{p}_{\theta})\in\mathbb{R}^{d},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(6)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.9" class="ltx_p">where in our implementation <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.7.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N=16" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>16</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N=16</annotation></semantics></math> and <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.8.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d=512" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>512</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">d=512</annotation></semantics></math> (constructed from stable marginals of the measurement statistics; see Methods).
Notably, PQKD does not require differentiating through the photonic hardware; it requires only sampling and a robust feature extractor <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px2.p2.9.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Phi" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Phi</annotation></semantics></math>.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Compressed convolution as a photonic-conditioned dictionary model.</h5>

<div id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1.5" class="ltx_p">We consider a <em id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1.5.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">convolutional neural network (CNN)</em> layer whose learnable weights are a 4th-order kernel tensor
<math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="W\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}\times C_{\mathrm{in}}\times k\times k}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>W</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>k</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">W\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}\times C_{\mathrm{in}}\times k\times k}</annotation></semantics></math> and bias
<math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">b\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}}</annotation></semantics></math>.
Here <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="C_{\mathrm{in}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C_{\mathrm{in}}</annotation></semantics></math> and <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="C_{\mathrm{out}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C_{\mathrm{out}}</annotation></semantics></math> denote the numbers of input and output channels, and
<math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="k\times k" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k\times k</annotation></semantics></math> is the spatial kernel size.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.7" class="ltx_p">PQKD replaces the fully trainable tensor <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="W" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>W</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">W</annotation></semantics></math> with a structured parameterisation that separates
<em id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.7.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">spatial structure</em> from <em id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.7.2" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">channel mixing</em>.
Specifically, we introduce <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>R</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">R</annotation></semantics></math> trainable spatial basis filters
<math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="B\in\mathbb{R}^{R\times k\times k}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>B</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>k</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">B\in\mathbb{R}^{R\times k\times k}</annotation></semantics></math> and a channel-mixing tensor
<math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}\times C_{\mathrm{in}}\times R}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}\times C_{\mathrm{in}}\times R}</annotation></semantics></math> such that, for each output channel <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="o" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>o</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">o</annotation></semantics></math>,
input channel <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.6.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="i" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>i</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">i</annotation></semantics></math>, and spatial indices <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.7.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\alpha,\beta\in\{1,\ldots,k\}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>α</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>k</mi><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha,\beta\in\{1,\ldots,k\}</annotation></semantics></math>,</p>
<table id="S2.E7" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E7.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="W_{o,i,\alpha,\beta}=\sum_{r=1}^{R}M_{o,i,r}\,B_{r,\alpha,\beta}." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>W</mi><mrow><mi>o</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>i</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>α</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow></msub><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><munderover><mo movablelimits="false">∑</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>R</mi></munderover><mrow><msub><mi>M</mi><mrow><mi>o</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>i</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>B</mi><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>α</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">W_{o,i,\alpha,\beta}=\sum_{r=1}^{R}M_{o,i,r}\,B_{r,\alpha,\beta}.</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(7)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.8" class="ltx_p">Equivalently, in tensor form one may write <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p2.8.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="W_{o,i,:,:}=\sum_{r=1}^{R}M_{o,i,r}\,B_{r,:,:}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>W</mi><mrow><mi>o</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>i</mi><mo>,</mo><mo rspace="0em">:</mo><mo>,</mo><mo>:</mo></mrow></msub><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><msubsup><mo>∑</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>R</mi></msubsup><mrow><msub><mi>M</mi><mrow><mi>o</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>i</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>B</mi><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>,</mo><mo rspace="0em">:</mo><mo>,</mo><mo>:</mo></mrow></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">W_{o,i,:,:}=\sum_{r=1}^{R}M_{o,i,r}\,B_{r,:,:}</annotation></semantics></math>, but
Eq. (<a href="#S2.E7" title="In Compressed convolution as a photonic-conditioned dictionary model. ‣ 2.1 Photonic quantum-enhanced knowledge distillation as a structured compression mechanism ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">7</span></a>) makes the index structure explicit.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p3.2" class="ltx_p">To avoid learning the large tensor <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p3.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>M</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M</annotation></semantics></math> directly, PQKD constrains it to be generated from the photonic feature <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p3.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> via a fixed linear map:</p>
<table id="S2.E8" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E8.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathrm{vec}(M)=A\,z(\theta)," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>vec</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>M</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>A</mi><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{vec}(M)=A\,z(\theta),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(8)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p3.4" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p3.3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="A\in\mathbb{R}^{(C_{\mathrm{out}}C_{\mathrm{in}}R)\times d}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>A</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A\in\mathbb{R}^{(C_{\mathrm{out}}C_{\mathrm{in}}R)\times d}</annotation></semantics></math> is fixed at initialisation (Methods). Equations (<a href="#S2.E7" title="In Compressed convolution as a photonic-conditioned dictionary model. ‣ 2.1 Photonic quantum-enhanced knowledge distillation as a structured compression mechanism ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">7</span></a>)–(<a href="#S2.E8" title="In Compressed convolution as a photonic-conditioned dictionary model. ‣ 2.1 Photonic quantum-enhanced knowledge distillation as a structured compression mechanism ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">8</span></a>) imply that the student convolutional kernels lie on a low-dimensional manifold controlled by <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p3.4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(B,\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>B</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(B,\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Parameter-count reduction.</h5>

<div id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.5" class="ltx_p">For a compressed convolutional layer, the number of trainable parameters is <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="Rk^{2}+C_{\mathrm{out}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mi>k</mi><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Rk^{2}+C_{\mathrm{out}}</annotation></semantics></math> for <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(B,b)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>B</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(B,b)</annotation></semantics></math>, plus the <em id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.5.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">global</em> photonic parameter budget <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo rspace="0em">dim</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dim(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> (shared across layers in our current design). In contrast, a dense kernel contains <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="C_{\mathrm{out}}C_{\mathrm{in}}k^{2}+C_{\mathrm{out}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mi>k</mi><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C_{\mathrm{out}}C_{\mathrm{in}}k^{2}+C_{\mathrm{out}}</annotation></semantics></math> trainable parameters. Ignoring the shared <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> term, the approximate per-layer compression factor is therefore</p>
<table id="S2.E9" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E9.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathrm{CR}_{\mathrm{conv}}\approx\frac{C_{\mathrm{out}}C_{\mathrm{in}}k^{2}}{Rk^{2}+C_{\mathrm{out}}}." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>CR</mi><mi>conv</mi></msub><mo>≈</mo><mfrac><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mi>k</mi><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mi>k</mi><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub></mrow></mfrac></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{CR}_{\mathrm{conv}}\approx\frac{C_{\mathrm{out}}C_{\mathrm{in}}k^{2}}{Rk^{2}+C_{\mathrm{out}}}.</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(9)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.7" class="ltx_p">When compressing multiple convolutional layers, the dominant trainable budget scales with <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.6.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sum_{\ell}R_{\ell}k_{\ell}^{2}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mo>∑</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi></msub><mrow><msub><mi>R</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msubsup><mi>k</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi><mn>2</mn></msubsup></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\sum_{\ell}R_{\ell}k_{\ell}^{2}</annotation></semantics></math> rather than <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.7.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sum_{\ell}C_{\mathrm{out}}^{(\ell)}C_{\mathrm{in}}^{(\ell)}k_{\ell}^{2}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mo>∑</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi></msub><mrow><msubsup><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msubsup><mi>C</mi><mi>in</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msubsup><mi>k</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi><mn>2</mn></msubsup></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\sum_{\ell}C_{\mathrm{out}}^{(\ell)}C_{\mathrm{in}}^{(\ell)}k_{\ell}^{2}</annotation></semantics></math>, enabling substantially larger end-to-end compression when the scheme is applied to the full convolutional stack.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px5" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Bilevel interpretation of photonic knowledge distillation.</h5>

<div id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px5.p1.2" class="ltx_p">PQKD optimises the student weights <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px5.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> and photonic parameters <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px5.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> under a coupled objective. A natural formulation is bilevel optimisation:</p>
<table id="S2.E10" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E10.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w^{\ast}(\theta)\in\arg\min_{w}\ \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{train}}_{\mathrm{KD}}(w,\theta),\qquad\theta^{\ast}\in\arg\min_{\theta}\ \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{val}}_{\mathrm{KD}}(w^{\ast}(\theta),\theta)," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><msup><mi>w</mi><mo>∗</mo></msup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>arg</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mrow><munder><mi>min</mi><mi>w</mi></munder><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><msubsup><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">ℒ</mi><mi>KD</mi><mi>train</mi></msubsup></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="2.167em">,</mo><mrow><msup><mi>θ</mi><mo>∗</mo></msup><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>arg</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mrow><munder><mi>min</mi><mi>θ</mi></munder><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><msubsup><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">ℒ</mi><mi>KD</mi><mi>val</mi></msubsup></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msup><mi>w</mi><mo>∗</mo></msup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w^{\ast}(\theta)\in\arg\min_{w}\ \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{train}}_{\mathrm{KD}}(w,\theta),\qquad\theta^{\ast}\in\arg\min_{\theta}\ \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{val}}_{\mathrm{KD}}(w^{\ast}(\theta),\theta),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(10)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px5.p1.5" class="ltx_p">where the outer objective uses a validation proxy that is robust to shot noise. Our training loop approximates Eq. (<a href="#S2.E10" title="In Bilevel interpretation of photonic knowledge distillation. ‣ 2.1 Photonic quantum-enhanced knowledge distillation as a structured compression mechanism ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">10</span></a>) by alternating (i) gradient-based updates for <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px5.p1.3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> and (ii) sampling-robust, gradient-free updates for <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px5.p1.4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> (Methods). In this view, the teacher supervises the student through softened logits, while the photonic module <em id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px5.p1.5.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">adapts the restricted student hypothesis class</em> by shaping <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px5.p1.5.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>, thereby selecting a compressed parameter manifold that best matches the teacher.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Finite-shot stability and noise propagation.</h5>

<div id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.3" class="ltx_p">Shot-limited sampling produces <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{p}_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{p}_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math> and hence a noisy feature <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{z}(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{z}(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>. For each bin <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\omega" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>ω</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\omega</annotation></semantics></math>, Hoeffding’s inequality gives</p>
<table id="S2.E11" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E11.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{P}\!\left(\left|\widehat{p}_{\theta}(\omega)-p_{\theta}(\omega)\right|\geq\epsilon\right)\leq 2\exp(-2S\epsilon^{2})." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mpadded style="width:0.441em;" width="0.441em"><mi>ℙ</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><mrow><mrow><mo>|</mo><mrow><mrow><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ω</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ω</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>|</mo></mrow><mo>≥</mo><mi>ϵ</mi></mrow><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>≤</mo><mrow><mn>2</mn><mo lspace="0.167em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mi>exp</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mn>2</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>S</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mi>ϵ</mi><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbb{P}\!\left(\left|\widehat{p}_{\theta}(\omega)-p_{\theta}(\omega)\right|\geq\epsilon\right)\leq 2\exp(-2S\epsilon^{2}).</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(11)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.4" class="ltx_p">If <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Phi" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Phi</annotation></semantics></math> is Lipschitz in the histogram (true for the marginal-based mapping used here away from degenerate normalisation; Methods), then with high probability</p>
<table id="S2.E12" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E12.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\|\widehat{z}(\theta)-z(\theta)\|_{2}\leq L_{\Phi}\,\|\widehat{p}_{\theta}-p_{\theta}\|_{1}=\mathcal{O}\!\left(\sqrt{\frac{K}{S}}\right)," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo><mrow><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo></mrow><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>≤</mo><mrow><msub><mi>L</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo><mrow><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo>−</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo></mrow><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mpadded style="width:0.654em;" width="0.654em"><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">𝒪</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><msqrt><mfrac><mi>K</mi><mi>S</mi></mfrac></msqrt><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\|\widehat{z}(\theta)-z(\theta)\|_{2}\leq L_{\Phi}\,\|\widehat{p}_{\theta}-p_{\theta}\|_{1}=\mathcal{O}\!\left(\sqrt{\frac{K}{S}}\right),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(12)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.10" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="K=|\Omega|" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>K</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">|</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">Ω</mi><mo stretchy="false">|</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">K=|\Omega|</annotation></semantics></math> is the effective number of histogram bins. Because <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.6.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>M</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M</annotation></semantics></math> depends linearly on <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.7.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>z</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z</annotation></semantics></math> and <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.8.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="W" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>W</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">W</annotation></semantics></math> is linear in <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.9.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>M</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M</annotation></semantics></math>, the reconstructed kernel is Lipschitz in <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.10.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>z</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z</annotation></semantics></math>:</p>
<table id="S2.E13" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E13.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\|W(B,\widehat{z})-W(B,z)\|_{F}\leq\|A\|_{2}\,\|B\|_{F}\,\|\widehat{z}-z\|_{2}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>W</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>B</mi><mo>,</mo><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>W</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>B</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>z</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo></mrow><mi>F</mi></msub><mo>≤</mo><mrow><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo><mi>A</mi><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo></mrow><mn>2</mn></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo><mi>B</mi><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo></mrow><mi>F</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>−</mo><mi>z</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">‖</mo></mrow><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\|W(B,\widehat{z})-W(B,z)\|_{F}\leq\|A\|_{2}\,\|B\|_{F}\,\|\widehat{z}-z\|_{2},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(13)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.11" class="ltx_p">and therefore weight and logit perturbations decay with <math id="S2.SS1.SSS0.Px6.p1.11.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> in a controlled manner. This provides a theoretical basis for the observed smooth degradation under reduced shot budgets and motivates feature smoothing (e.g., exponential moving averages (EMA)) as a variance-reduction mechanism during training.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section id="S2.SS2" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">2.2 </span>Training and validation dynamics</h3>

<div id="S2.SS2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS2.p1.4" class="ltx_p">We evaluate PQKD on MNIST, Fashion-MNIST and CIFAR-10 using a unified experimental protocol (Methods; Supplementary Information). The teacher is a three-layer convolutional network, and the PQKD student preserves the same overall structure but compresses the first two convolutional layers by restricting their kernels to a low-dimensional manifold generated by a shot-limited photonic module. This reduces the effective parameter count from <math id="S2.SS2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sim 2.25\times 10^{5}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi></mi><mo>∼</mo><mrow><mn>2.25</mn><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><msup><mn>10</mn><mn>5</mn></msup></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\sim 2.25\times 10^{5}</annotation></semantics></math> (teacher) to <math id="S2.SS2.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sim 1.50\times 10^{5}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi></mi><mo>∼</mo><mrow><mn>1.50</mn><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><msup><mn>10</mn><mn>5</mn></msup></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\sim 1.50\times 10^{5}</annotation></semantics></math> (student), while introducing only 45 trainable photonic parameters <math id="S2.SS2.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math>, corresponding to <math id="S2.SS2.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="\sim\!1.5\times" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo rspace="0.108em">∼</mo><mn>1.5</mn><mo lspace="0.222em">×</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\sim\!1.5\times</annotation></semantics></math> compression. We focus here on partial convolutional compression to isolate training and generalisation dynamics; full-network compression and scaling results are presented in the next subsection.</p>
</div>
<figure id="S2.T1" class="ltx_table">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption" style="font-size:70%;"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_table">Table 1: </span><span id="S2.T1.35.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">PQKD performance and optimisation (Opt.) diagnostics.
