</figure>
<figure id="S2.F2" class="ltx_figure"><img src="2603.14898v1/x2.png" id="S2.F2.g1" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_square" width="660" height="645" alt="Refer to caption">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 2: </span><span id="S2.F2.7.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Training and validation dynamics across datasets.</span>
Mean <math id="S2.F2.2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pm" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mo>±</mo><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\pm</annotation></semantics></math> s.d. over five independent runs comparing the teacher (green) and PQKD student (blue) on MNIST <span id="S2.F2.8.2" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">a</span> , Fashion-MNIST <span id="S2.F2.9.3" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">b</span>, and CIFAR-10 <span id="S2.F2.10.4" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">c</span>. Top row: training accuracy. Middle row: validation accuracy. Bottom row: cross-entropy (CE) loss for training (solid) and validation (dashed)
</figcaption>
</figure>
<div id="S2.SS2.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS2.p2.1" class="ltx_p">Training and validation dynamics are summarised in Fig. <a href="#S2.F2" title="Figure 2 ‣ 2.2 Training and validation dynamics ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a> (mean <math id="S2.SS2.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pm" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mo>±</mo><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\pm</annotation></semantics></math> s.d. over five independent runs), with aggregate metrics reported in Table <a href="#S2.T1" title="Table 1 ‣ 2.2 Training and validation dynamics ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a>. On MNIST and Fashion-MNIST, the teacher rapidly reaches near-saturated training accuracy, yet exhibits comparatively larger run-to-run fluctuations in validation accuracy and validation CE loss, consistent with over-parameterisation for these tasks. PQKD mitigates this behaviour: under a substantially reduced parameter budget, the student maintains competitive training performance while improving validation stability and achieving favourable validation CE compared with the teacher (Table <a href="#S2.T1" title="Table 1 ‣ 2.2 Training and validation dynamics ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a>). These trends indicate that distillation, combined with the compressed photonic kernel parameterisation, regularises the effective hypothesis space and improves generalisation beyond what is captured by accuracy alone.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS2.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS2.p3.1" class="ltx_p">For CIFAR-10, the teacher remains stronger in both training and validation accuracy, reflecting increased task complexity under the same compression budget. Nevertheless, PQKD optimisation remains well behaved across datasets: the photonic optimisation diagnostic <math id="S2.SS2.p3.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Delta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Delta</annotation></semantics></math> is consistently positive (shown in Table <a href="#S2.T1" title="Table 1 ‣ 2.2 Training and validation dynamics ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a>), indicating systematic progress of the photonic module during training. Overall, Fig. <a href="#S2.F2" title="Figure 2 ‣ 2.2 Training and validation dynamics ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a> and Table <a href="#S2.T1" title="Table 1 ‣ 2.2 Training and validation dynamics ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a> show that PQKD can reduce model size while stabilising validation behaviour in regimes where an uncompressed network exhibits signatures of over-fitting.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S2.SS3" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">2.3 </span>Scaling compression from partial to full convolutional compression</h3>

<figure id="S2.F3" class="ltx_figure"><img src="2603.14898v1/x3.png" id="S2.F3.g1" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_landscape" width="660" height="426" alt="Refer to caption">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 3: </span><span id="S2.F3.14.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Scaling photonic-conditioned convolutional compression across network scope and teacher capacity on MNIST.</span>
Validation accuracy drop relative to the corresponding teacher in percentage points, plotted against the overall compression factor of the compressed network (bottom axis; <span id="S2.F3.15.2" class="ltx_text ltx_markedasmath ltx_font_typewriter">compression_x</span>). Columns report the compression scope: <span id="S2.F3.16.3" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Conv1</span> (left), <span id="S2.F3.17.4" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Conv1+Conv2</span> (middle), and <span id="S2.F3.18.5" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">All Convs</span> (right). Rows correspond to three teacher widths, <math id="S2.F3.6.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(c_{1},c_{2},c_{3})\in\{(32,64,128),(48,96,128),(64,128,128)\}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>c</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>c</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>c</mi><mn>3</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>32</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>64</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>128</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>48</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>96</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>128</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>64</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>128</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>128</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(c_{1},c_{2},c_{3})\in\{(32,64,128),(48,96,128),(64,128,128)\}</annotation></semantics></math>, with each row aggregating all configurations for that teacher. Marker shape encodes the photonic parameter dimension <math id="S2.F3.7.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim(\theta)\in\{15,30,45\}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0em">dim</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>15</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>30</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>45</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dim(\theta)\in\{15,30,45\}</annotation></semantics></math>, and marker size encodes the kernel-manifold rank <math id="S2.F3.8.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R\in\{4,8,12\}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>4</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>8</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>12</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">R\in\{4,8,12\}</annotation></semantics></math>. Faint markers show individual seeds, while opaque markers and vertical bars indicate the mean and one standard deviation across seeds.</figcaption>
</figure>
<div id="S2.SS3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS3.p1.1" class="ltx_p">To assess whether PQKD remains effective under increasingly aggressive structural constraints, we progressively expanded the scope of convolutional compression from early to deep network stages. Specifically, we considered three regimes: compressing only the first convolutional layer (<span id="S2.SS3.p1.1.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Conv1</span>), compressing the first two convolutional layers (<span id="S2.SS3.p1.1.2" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Conv1+Conv2</span>), and compressing the entire convolutional stack (<span id="S2.SS3.p1.1.3" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Conv1–Conv3</span>). This controlled progression isolates how far the structured parameterisation defined in Eqs. (<a href="#S2.E7" title="In Compressed convolution as a photonic-conditioned dictionary model. ‣ 2.1 Photonic quantum-enhanced knowledge distillation as a structured compression mechanism ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">7</span></a>)–(<a href="#S2.E8" title="In Compressed convolution as a photonic-conditioned dictionary model. ‣ 2.1 Photonic quantum-enhanced knowledge distillation as a structured compression mechanism ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">8</span></a>) can be pushed before accuracy degrades, and whether knowledge distillation can stabilise learning on increasingly low-dimensional kernel manifolds.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS3.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS3.p2.3" class="ltx_p">Figure <a href="#S2.F3" title="Figure 3 ‣ 2.3 Scaling compression from partial to full convolutional compression ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a> summarises the resulting compression–accuracy landscapes across compression scopes and teacher capacities. Each column corresponds to a compression scope, while rows aggregate results for three teacher widths, <math id="S2.SS3.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(c_{1},c_{2},c_{3})\in\{(32,64,128),(48,96,128),(64,128,128)\}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>c</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>c</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>c</mi><mn>3</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>32</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>64</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>128</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>48</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>96</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>128</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>64</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>128</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>128</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(c_{1},c_{2},c_{3})\in\{(32,64,128),(48,96,128),(64,128,128)\}</annotation></semantics></math>. The vertical axis reports the test accuracy drop relative to the corresponding teacher, while the horizontal axis reports the compression factor restricted to the compressed subnetwork. The overall compression factor of the full model is shown on the top axis for reference. Marker shape encodes the photonic parameter budget <math id="S2.SS3.p2.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo rspace="0em">dim</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dim(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> and marker size encodes the basis rank <math id="S2.SS3.p2.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>R</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">R</annotation></semantics></math>, enabling the joint effects of spatial expressivity and photonic conditioning capacity to be visualised.</p>
</div>

<span id="S2.T2.57.47.5.1.1.1" class="ltx_p"><span id="S2.T2.57.47.5.1.1.1.1" class="ltx_text" style="font-size:70%;">(</span><math id="S2.T2.57.47.5.1.1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pm" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mo mathsize="0.700em">±</mo><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\pm</annotation></semantics></math><span id="S2.T2.57.47.5.1.1.1.2" class="ltx_text" style="font-size:70%;"> 0.11)</span></span>

</table>
</figure>
<div id="S2.SS3.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS3.p3.1" class="ltx_p">When compressing only <span id="S2.SS3.p3.1.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Conv1</span>, the end-to-end reduction in trainable parameters is modest, as deeper convolutional layers and the classifier continue to dominate the student capacity. Nevertheless, across all teacher widths, the PQKD student closely matches—and in some cases marginally exceeds—the teacher’s validation accuracy (Table <a href="#S2.T2" title="Table 2 ‣ 2.3 Scaling compression from partial to full convolutional compression ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a>), with negligible accuracy drop. This indicates that early-stage feature extraction can be represented efficiently by a low-rank photonic-conditioned basis without loss of discriminative power, and that the remaining dense layers are sufficient to absorb residual modelling capacity.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS3.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS3.p4.5" class="ltx_p">Extending compression to <span id="S2.SS3.p4.5.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Conv1+Conv2</span> substantially increases the fraction of parameters subject to structured constraint, leading to clearer reductions in trainable parameters while preserving strong performance. In this regime, the compression–accuracy trade-off becomes explicit and is jointly controlled by the basis rank <math id="S2.SS3.p4.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>R</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">R</annotation></semantics></math> and the photonic parameter budget <math id="S2.SS3.p4.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo rspace="0em">dim</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dim(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>, which together determine the dimensionality of the admissible kernel manifold. Across all teacher widths, PQKD maintains validation accuracy within <math id="S2.SS3.p4.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sim" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mo>∼</mo><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\sim</annotation></semantics></math>0.2–0.3% of the teacher at overall compression factors of <math id="S2.SS3.p4.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="C_{x}\approx 1.25" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>x</mi></msub><mo>≈</mo><mn>1.25</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C_{x}\approx 1.25</annotation></semantics></math>–<math id="S2.SS3.p4.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="1.50" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>1.50</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1.50</annotation></semantics></math>, demonstrating that photonic conditioning and distillation can stabilise learning even when multiple convolutional stages are constrained.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS3.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS3.p5.2" class="ltx_p">Compressing <span id="S2.SS3.p5.2.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">all convolutional layers</span> yields the largest parameter reductions and exposes a clear compression frontier. In this regime, decreasing the basis rank <math id="S2.SS3.p5.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>R</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">R</annotation></semantics></math> increases compression at the cost of higher accuracy drop, while increasing <math id="S2.SS3.p5.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>R</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">R</annotation></semantics></math> recovers accuracy with diminishing returns in parameter count. Importantly, even at extreme compression factors exceeding two orders of magnitude in the convolutional subnetwork, PQKD retains stable training and converges to well-defined operating points, rather than exhibiting catastrophic degradation. This behaviour indicates that the combination of photonic-conditioned structured parameterisation and knowledge distillation effectively regularises the optimisation landscape under severe dimensionality reduction.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS3.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS3.p6.1" class="ltx_p">Representative operating points for each compression scope and teacher width are reported in Table <a href="#S2.T2" title="Table 2 ‣ 2.3 Scaling compression from partial to full convolutional compression ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a>. Together, these results demonstrate that PQKD supports a smooth and controllable transition from partial to full convolutional compression, enabling substantial reductions in trainable parameters while preserving accuracy across a wide range of model capacities.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S2.SS4" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">2.4 </span>Robustness to shot noise and hardware-relevant perturbations</h3>

<div id="S2.SS4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS4.p1.5" class="ltx_p">Finally, we probe robustness to stochasticity intrinsic to near-term photonic sampling and to perturbations that capture hardware-relevant variability. In PQKD, the photonic module is queried with a finite measurement budget <math id="S2.SS4.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> to produce an empirical histogram <math id="S2.SS4.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{p}_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{p}_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math>, which is then mapped deterministically to a conditioning feature <math id="S2.SS4.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{z}(\theta)=\Phi(\widehat{p}_{\theta})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{z}(\theta)=\Phi(\widehat{p}_{\theta})</annotation></semantics></math> (Methods; Supplementary Note S5). Finite-shot sampling therefore induces a stochastic feature perturbation <math id="S2.SS4.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{z}(\theta)-z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{z}(\theta)-z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>, where <math id="S2.SS4.p1.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)=\Phi(p_{\theta})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)=\Phi(p_{\theta})</annotation></semantics></math> is the infinite-shot feature. Under a Lipschitz assumption for the histogram-to-feature map (Eq. (<a href="#S3.E51" title="In Propagation to mixing coefficients and convolution kernels. ‣ S3.3 Finite-shot noise propagation ‣ S3 Supplementary Note 3: Theory—expressivity, approximation, and stability ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S51</span></a>)), standard multinomial concentration implies</p>
<table id="S2.E14" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E14.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{E}\!\left[\left\lVert\widehat{z}(\theta)-z(\theta)\right\rVert_{2}\right]=\mathcal{O}\!\left(L_{\Phi}\sqrt{\frac{K}{S}}\right)," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mpadded style="width:0.497em;" width="0.497em"><mi>𝔼</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>[</mo><msub><mrow><mo>‖</mo><mrow><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>‖</mo></mrow><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>]</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mpadded style="width:0.654em;" width="0.654em"><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">𝒪</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>L</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msqrt><mfrac><mi>K</mi><mi>S</mi></mfrac></msqrt></mrow><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbb{E}\!\left[\left\lVert\widehat{z}(\theta)-z(\theta)\right\rVert_{2}\right]=\mathcal{O}\!\left(L_{\Phi}\sqrt{\frac{K}{S}}\right),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(14)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS4.p1.10" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S2.SS4.p1.6.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="K" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>K</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">K</annotation></semantics></math> is the effective number of histogram bins used by <math id="S2.SS4.p1.7.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Phi" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Phi</annotation></semantics></math> (here <math id="S2.SS4.p1.8.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="K{=}512" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>K</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>512</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">K{=}512</annotation></semantics></math> for two concatenated 256-bin marginals). Equation (<a href="#S2.E14" title="In 2.4 Robustness to shot noise and hardware-relevant perturbations ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">14</span></a>) predicts a characteristic <math id="S2.SS4.p1.9.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="1/\sqrt{S}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><msqrt><mi>S</mi></msqrt></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1/\sqrt{S}</annotation></semantics></math> scaling of the shot-induced feature noise, and hence a saturation of performance as <math id="S2.SS4.p1.10.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> increases.</p>
</div>
<figure id="S2.F4" class="ltx_figure"><img src="2603.14898v1/x4.png" id="S2.F4.g1" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_landscape" width="529" height="412" alt="Refer to caption">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 4: </span><span id="S2.F4.14.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Shot-limited scaling of the photonic conditioning signal in PQKD.</span>
Increase in test accuracy due to the photonic feature, <math id="S2.F4.7.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta\,\mathrm{test\ acc}\equiv\mathrm{acc}(z)-\mathrm{acc}(z{=}0)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>test</mi><mo lspace="0.500em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>acc</mi></mrow><mo>≡</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>acc</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>z</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>acc</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\delta\,\mathrm{test\ acc}\equiv\mathrm{acc}(z)-\mathrm{acc}(z{=}0)</annotation></semantics></math>, as a function of the photonic measurement budget <math id="S2.F4.8.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> (shots), comparing EMA aggregation of the feature across epochs (blue) with no EMA (orange). Solid curves show the mean over random seeds and shaded bands denote <math id="S2.F4.9.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pm 1" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo>±</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\pm 1</annotation></semantics></math> s.d. The dashed curves are fits to the shot-noise model <math id="S2.F4.10.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(S)=\delta_{\infty}-k/\sqrt{S}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>S</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>δ</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">∞</mi></msub><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>/</mo><msqrt><mi>S</mi></msqrt></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\delta(S)=\delta_{\infty}-k/\sqrt{S}</annotation></semantics></math>, consistent with multinomial histogram fluctuations propagating through a Lipschitz feature map, which predicts a <math id="S2.F4.11.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="1/\sqrt{S}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><msqrt><mi>S</mi></msqrt></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1/\sqrt{S}</annotation></semantics></math> decay of stochastic feature perturbations and a corresponding saturation of performance at large <math id="S2.F4.12.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math>.</figcaption>
</figure>
<div id="S2.SS4.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS4.p2.6" class="ltx_p">To test this prediction, we sweep the shot budget <math id="S2.SS4.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> used to form the photonic conditioning signal during training and evaluation, while holding the student architecture and optimisation schedule fixed. We additionally include two perturbation families that emulate hardware variability: additive feature corruption <math id="S2.SS4.p2.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{z}\leftarrow\widehat{z}+\eta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo stretchy="false">←</mo><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>+</mo><mi>η</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{z}\leftarrow\widehat{z}+\eta</annotation></semantics></math> with <math id="S2.SS4.p2.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\eta\sim\mathcal{N}(0,\sigma_{z}^{2}I)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>η</mi><mo>∼</mo><mrow><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">𝒩</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mrow><msubsup><mi>σ</mi><mi>z</mi><mn>2</mn></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\eta\sim\mathcal{N}(0,\sigma_{z}^{2}I)</annotation></semantics></math>, and mild parameter drift <math id="S2.SS4.p2.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta\leftarrow\theta+\xi" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">←</mo><mrow><mi>θ</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>ξ</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta\leftarrow\theta+\xi</annotation></semantics></math> between epochs with <math id="S2.SS4.p2.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\xi\sim\mathcal{N}(0,\sigma_{\theta}^{2}I)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>ξ</mi><mo>∼</mo><mrow><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">𝒩</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mrow><msubsup><mi>σ</mi><mi>θ</mi><mn>2</mn></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\xi\sim\mathcal{N}(0,\sigma_{\theta}^{2}I)</annotation></semantics></math> (Methods). For each condition we also compare a simple variance-reduction mechanism, exponential moving average (EMA) smoothing of the photonic feature across epochs, which is expected to attenuate high-frequency fluctuations in <math id="S2.SS4.p2.6.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{z}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{z}</annotation></semantics></math>.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS4.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS4.p3.3" class="ltx_p">Figure <a href="#S2.F4" title="Figure 4 ‣ 2.4 Robustness to shot noise and hardware-relevant perturbations ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">4</span></a> reports an <em id="S2.SS4.p3.3.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">ablation</em> that isolates the contribution of the photonic feature by subtracting a matched “no-photonic” baseline:
<math id="S2.SS4.p3.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta\,\mathrm{test\ acc}\equiv\mathrm{acc}(z)-\mathrm{acc}(z{=}0)," display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>test</mi><mo lspace="0.500em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>acc</mi></mrow><mo>≡</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>acc</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>z</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>acc</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\delta\,\mathrm{test\ acc}\equiv\mathrm{acc}(z)-\mathrm{acc}(z{=}0),</annotation></semantics></math>
plotted as a function of the shot budget <math id="S2.SS4.p3.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math>.
The dependence on <math id="S2.SS4.p3.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> is well captured by the theory-motivated form</p>
<table id="S2.E15" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E15.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(S)=\delta_{\infty}-\frac{k}{\sqrt{S}}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>S</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>δ</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">∞</mi></msub><mo>−</mo><mfrac><mi>k</mi><msqrt><mi>S</mi></msqrt></mfrac></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\delta(S)=\delta_{\infty}-\frac{k}{\sqrt{S}},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
