</div>
<div id="S4.SS4.SSS1.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.SS4.SSS1.p2.2" class="ltx_p">Unless stated otherwise, we used <math id="S4.SS4.SSS1.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau=3" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>3</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\tau=3</annotation></semantics></math> and <math id="S4.SS4.SSS1.p2.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\lambda=0.5" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>λ</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0.5</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\lambda=0.5</annotation></semantics></math>.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S4.SS4.SSS2" class="ltx_subsubsection">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">4.4.2 </span>Alternating optimisation (student weights and photonic parameters)</h4>

<div id="S4.SS4.SSS2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.SS4.SSS2.p1.5" class="ltx_p">Training proceeds in two nested loops:</p>
<ul id="S4.I5" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="S4.I5.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="S4.I5.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.I5.i1.p1.3" class="ltx_p"><span id="S4.I5.i1.p1.3.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Student update:</span> with the current photonic feature <math id="S4.I5.i1.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> fixed, update student weights <math id="S4.I5.i1.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> (basis filters, biases, and classifier head) using Adam on <math id="S4.I5.i1.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathcal{L}_{\mathrm{KD}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">ℒ</mi><mi>KD</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathcal{L}_{\mathrm{KD}}</annotation></semantics></math>.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="S4.I5.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="S4.I5.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.I5.i2.p1.3" class="ltx_p"><span id="S4.I5.i2.p1.3.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Photonic update:</span> update <math id="S4.I5.i2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> using a sampling-robust, gradient-free method based on a validation proxy of <math id="S4.I5.i2.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathcal{L}_{\mathrm{KD}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">ℒ</mi><mi>KD</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathcal{L}_{\mathrm{KD}}</annotation></semantics></math> while holding <math id="S4.I5.i2.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> fixed.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p id="S4.SS4.SSS2.p1.4" class="ltx_p">We used <math id="S4.SS4.SSS2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="100" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>100</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">100</annotation></semantics></math> epochs for the teacher and <math id="S4.SS4.SSS2.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="100" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>100</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">100</annotation></semantics></math> epochs for the student. For photonic updates we performed <math id="S4.SS4.SSS2.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\texttt{theta\_updates\_per\_epoch}=10" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mtext class="ltx_mathvariant_monospace">theta_updates_per_epoch</mtext><mo>=</mo><mn>10</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\texttt{theta\_updates\_per\_epoch}=10</annotation></semantics></math> steps per student epoch. The shot budget <math id="S4.SS4.SSS2.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> was held fixed (“shots kept”) unless explicitly varied in noise studies.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S4.SS4.SSS3" class="ltx_subsubsection">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">4.4.3 </span>Photonic parameter updates (SPSA)</h4>

<div id="S4.SS4.SSS3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.SS4.SSS3.p1.4" class="ltx_p">To avoid backpropagation through shot-noisy sampling, we used simultaneous perturbation stochastic approximation (SPSA). At step <math id="S4.SS4.SSS3.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="k" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>k</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math>, draw a Rademacher perturbation vector <math id="S4.SS4.SSS3.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Delta_{k}\in\{\pm 1\}^{\dim(\theta)}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi>k</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mrow><mo>±</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0em">dim</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Delta_{k}\in\{\pm 1\}^{\dim(\theta)}</annotation></semantics></math> and evaluate a validation objective <math id="S4.SS4.SSS3.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">J(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> (the KD loss computed on a fixed number of validation batches) at
<math id="S4.SS4.SSS3.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta_{k}^{\pm}=\theta_{k}\pm c\,\Delta_{k}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msubsup><mi>θ</mi><mi>k</mi><mo>±</mo></msubsup><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi>k</mi></msub><mo>±</mo><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta_{k}^{\pm}=\theta_{k}\pm c\,\Delta_{k}</annotation></semantics></math>.
The gradient estimate is</p>
<table id="S4.E21" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S4.E21.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{g}_{k}=\frac{J(\theta_{k}^{+})-J(\theta_{k}^{-})}{2c}\,\Delta_{k}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>g</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>k</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mfrac><mrow><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msubsup><mi>θ</mi><mi>k</mi><mo>+</mo></msubsup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msubsup><mi>θ</mi><mi>k</mi><mo>−</mo></msubsup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mfrac><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{g}_{k}=\frac{J(\theta_{k}^{+})-J(\theta_{k}^{-})}{2c}\,\Delta_{k},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(21)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S4.SS4.SSS3.p1.6" class="ltx_p">and the update is <math id="S4.SS4.SSS3.p1.5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta_{k+1}=\theta_{k}-a\,\widehat{g}_{k}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>θ</mi><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>+</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi>k</mi></msub><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>g</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta_{k+1}=\theta_{k}-a\,\widehat{g}_{k}</annotation></semantics></math>, with clipping to a bounded interval to prevent parameter blow-up. We used constant step sizes <math id="S4.SS4.SSS3.p1.6.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(a,c)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(a,c)</annotation></semantics></math> in the main experiments and verified that results were qualitatively robust to moderate changes in these hyperparameters.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S4.SS4.SSS4" class="ltx_subsubsection">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">4.4.4 </span>Feature smoothing and stability</h4>

<div id="S4.SS4.SSS4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.SS4.SSS4.p1.3" class="ltx_p">To reduce shot-to-shot variance, we optionally applied exponential moving average (EMA) smoothing to the photonic feature:</p>
<table id="S4.E22" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S4.E22.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\bar{z}\leftarrow\beta\,\bar{z}+(1-\beta)\,z(\theta)," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover><mo stretchy="false">←</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>β</mi><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bar{z}\leftarrow\beta\,\bar{z}+(1-\beta)\,z(\theta),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(22)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S4.SS4.SSS4.p1.2" class="ltx_p">and used <math id="S4.SS4.SSS4.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\bar{z}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bar{z}</annotation></semantics></math> as the conditioning signal for the student forward pass. We used <math id="S4.SS4.SSS4.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\beta=0.9" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>β</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0.9</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\beta=0.9</annotation></semantics></math> unless stated otherwise.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section id="S4.SS5" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">4.5 </span>Noise impact experiments</h3>

<div id="S4.SS5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.SS5.p1.4" class="ltx_p">To probe robustness under hardware-relevant noise, we conducted three perturbation studies:</p>
<ol id="S4.I6" class="ltx_enumerate">
<li id="S4.I6.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">1.</span> 
<div id="S4.I6.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.I6.i1.p1.1" class="ltx_p"><span id="S4.I6.i1.p1.1.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Finite-shot noise:</span> vary <math id="S4.I6.i1.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> (shots per feature evaluation) while keeping all other hyperparameters fixed.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="S4.I6.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">2.</span> 
<div id="S4.I6.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.I6.i2.p1.2" class="ltx_p"><span id="S4.I6.i2.p1.2.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Feature corruption:</span> add zero-mean Gaussian noise to the photonic feature, <math id="S4.I6.i2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tilde{z}=z+\eta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>~</mo></mover><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>η</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\tilde{z}=z+\eta</annotation></semantics></math> with <math id="S4.I6.i2.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\eta\sim\mathcal{N}(0,\sigma_{z}^{2}I)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>η</mi><mo>∼</mo><mrow><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">𝒩</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mrow><msubsup><mi>σ</mi><mi>z</mi><mn>2</mn></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\eta\sim\mathcal{N}(0,\sigma_{z}^{2}I)</annotation></semantics></math>, to emulate readout fluctuations or unmodelled drift in feature statistics.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="S4.I6.i3" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">3.</span> 
<div id="S4.I6.i3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.I6.i3.p1.2" class="ltx_p"><span id="S4.I6.i3.p1.2.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Parameter drift:</span> perturb photonic parameters between epochs, <math id="S4.I6.i3.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta\leftarrow\theta+\xi" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">←</mo><mrow><mi>θ</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>ξ</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta\leftarrow\theta+\xi</annotation></semantics></math> with <math id="S4.I6.i3.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\xi\sim\mathcal{N}(0,\sigma_{\theta}^{2}I)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>ξ</mi><mo>∼</mo><mrow><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">𝒩</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mrow><msubsup><mi>σ</mi><mi>θ</mi><mn>2</mn></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\xi\sim\mathcal{N}(0,\sigma_{\theta}^{2}I)</annotation></semantics></math>, to emulate slow hardware drift.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ol>
<p id="S4.SS5.p1.3" class="ltx_p">Accuracy and loss were reported as a function of <math id="S4.SS5.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math>, <math id="S4.SS5.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma_{z}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>σ</mi><mi>z</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\sigma_{z}</annotation></semantics></math>, and <math id="S4.SS5.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>σ</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\sigma_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math>, and compared with and without EMA smoothing to quantify stability improvements.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S4.SS6" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">4.6 </span>Evaluation metrics and compression accounting</h3>

<section id="S4.SS6.SSS0.Px1" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Accuracy.</h5>

<div id="S4.SS6.SSS0.Px1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.SS6.SSS0.Px1.p1.1" class="ltx_p">We report top-1 classification accuracy on validation and held-out test sets.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S4.SS6.SSS0.Px2" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Trainable parameter counts.</h5>

<div id="S4.SS6.SSS0.Px2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.SS6.SSS0.Px2.p1.2" class="ltx_p">Compression ratios are computed using the number of <em id="S4.SS6.SSS0.Px2.p1.2.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">trainable</em> parameters. Fixed matrices <math id="S4.SS6.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="A" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>A</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A</annotation></semantics></math> used to generate mixing coefficients are not trainable and are not counted toward adaptation capacity. When reporting end-to-end compression, we include the photonic parameter budget <math id="S4.SS6.SSS0.Px2.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo rspace="0em">dim</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dim(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> as trainable parameters. We separately report convolution-only compression ratios (restricted to the convolutional stack) and full-model compression ratios (including the classifier head).</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section id="S4.SS7" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">4.7 </span>Implementation details and reproducibility</h3>

<section id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px1" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Software and hardware.</h5>

<div id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px1.p1.1" class="ltx_p">Classical models were implemented in PyTorch and trained on a CUDA-capable GPU; the PQKD model was also inferred using a CUDA-capable GPU. Photonic sampling was executed via the ORCA simulator backend in CUDA-Q (matching the circuit-level sampling interface used in our pipeline); when available, the same experiment can be run against ORCA Computing’s <span id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px1.p1.1.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter">ptseries</span> backend with identical sampling calls and output formatting, enabling drop-in replacement of the simulator by hardware-relevant photonic sampling.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Hyperparameters.</h5>

<div id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.8" class="ltx_p">Unless otherwise stated, we used: batch size 64; Adam learning rate <math id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="10^{-3}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msup><mn>10</mn><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>3</mn></mrow></msup><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">10^{-3}</annotation></semantics></math> for both teacher and student; dropout <math id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p=0.25" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0.25</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">p=0.25</annotation></semantics></math>; temperature <math id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau=3" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>3</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\tau=3</annotation></semantics></math>; distillation mixing <math id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\lambda=0.5" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>λ</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0.5</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\lambda=0.5</annotation></semantics></math>; <math id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N=16" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>16</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N=16</annotation></semantics></math> photonic modes; feature dimension <math id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.6.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d=512" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>512</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">d=512</annotation></semantics></math>; <math id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.7.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\texttt{theta\_updates\_per\_epoch}=10" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mtext class="ltx_mathvariant_monospace">theta_updates_per_epoch</mtext><mo>=</mo><mn>10</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\texttt{theta\_updates\_per\_epoch}=10</annotation></semantics></math>; and a fixed shot budget <math id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.8.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> (held constant within an experiment).</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px3" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Randomness control.</h5>

<div id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S4.SS7.SSS0.Px3.p1.1" class="ltx_p">We fixed random seeds for dataset splits, network initialisation, and stochastic optimisers. For each configuration, we used the same split indices and repeated runs with multiple seeds where noted; summary statistics (mean and standard deviation) are reported when multiple runs were performed.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
</section>

<section id="S1a" class="ltx_section">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">S1 </span>Supplementary Note 1: Fundamentals</h2>

<section id="S1.SS1" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S1.1 </span>Knowledge distillation</h3>

<div id="S1.SS1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS1.p1.8" class="ltx_p">Knowledge distillation <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">hinton2015distilling</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">buciluǎ2006model</span>]</cite> trains a compact student model to approximate the predictive behaviour of a stronger teacher by using the teacher’s <em id="S1.SS1.p1.8.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">soft</em> class probabilities as supervision. Let the teacher produce logits <math id="S1.SS1.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="t(x)\in\mathbb{R}^{C}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>t</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mi>C</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">t(x)\in\mathbb{R}^{C}</annotation></semantics></math> and the student produce logits <math id="S1.SS1.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="s(x;w,\theta)\in\mathbb{R}^{C}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo>;</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mi>C</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">s(x;w,\theta)\in\mathbb{R}^{C}</annotation></semantics></math> for an input <math id="S1.SS1.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>x</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">x</annotation></semantics></math>, where <math id="S1.SS1.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="C" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>C</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C</annotation></semantics></math> is the number of classes, <math id="S1.SS1.p1.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> denotes the trainable student parameters, and <math id="S1.SS1.p1.6.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> denotes the photonic parameters that condition the student through the feature <math id="S1.SS1.p1.7.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> described in Supplementary Note <a href="#S2a" title="S2 Supplementary Note 2: Definition of Photonic Quantum Knowledge Distillation ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S2</span></a>. For temperature <math id="S1.SS1.p1.8.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau&gt;0" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\tau&gt;0</annotation></semantics></math>, define softened distributions</p>
<table id="S1.E1" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S1.E1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{T}^{(\tau)}(x)=\operatorname{softmax}\!\left(\frac{t(x)}{\tau}\right),\qquad p_{S}^{(\tau)}(x;w,\theta)=\operatorname{softmax}\!\left(\frac{s(x;w,\theta)}{\tau}\right)." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>T</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mpadded style="width:3.720em;" width="3.720em"><mi>softmax</mi></mpadded><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><mfrac><mrow><mi>t</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mi>τ</mi></mfrac><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="2.167em">,</mo><mrow><mrow><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>S</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo>;</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mpadded style="width:3.720em;" width="3.720em"><mi>softmax</mi></mpadded><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><mfrac><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo>;</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mi>τ</mi></mfrac><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">p_{T}^{(\tau)}(x)=\operatorname{softmax}\!\left(\frac{t(x)}{\tau}\right),\qquad p_{S}^{(\tau)}(x;w,\theta)=\operatorname{softmax}\!\left(\frac{s(x;w,\theta)}{\tau}\right).</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S1)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S1.SS1.p1.9" class="ltx_p">Larger <math id="S1.SS1.p1.9.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>τ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\tau</annotation></semantics></math> increases the entropy of the distributions, revealing “dark knowledge” in the teacher’s inter-class similarities, which can be particularly informative when the student hypothesis class is strongly constrained by compression.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.SS1.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS1.p2.8" class="ltx_p">We optimise the student using a standard distillation objective that interpolates between hard-label supervision and teacher matching:</p>

<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_left ltx_eqn_cell"><math id="S1.E2X.3.2.2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\displaystyle\ \mathbb{E}_{(x,y)}\Big[\lambda\,\operatorname{CE}\!\big(y,\ </table>
<p id="S1.SS1.p2.7" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S1.SS1.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\lambda\in[0,1]" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>λ</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\lambda\in[0,1]</annotation></semantics></math> controls the mixture and <math id="S1.SS1.p2.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\operatorname{CE}(y,p)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>CE</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>y</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>p</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\operatorname{CE}(y,p)</annotation></semantics></math> denotes cross-entropy between the one-hot label <math id="S1.SS1.p2.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>y</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">y</annotation></semantics></math> and predicted probability vector <math id="S1.SS1.p2.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>p</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">p</annotation></semantics></math>. The <math id="S1.SS1.p2.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau^{2}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msup><mi>τ</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\tau^{2}</annotation></semantics></math> factor preserves gradient magnitudes as <math id="S1.SS1.p2.6.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>τ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\tau</annotation></semantics></math> varies, because the softmax gradients scale approximately as <math id="S1.SS1.p2.7.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="1/\tau" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><mi>τ</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1/\tau</annotation></semantics></math>; without this factor, the distillation signal would diminish at higher temperatures.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.SS1.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS1.p3.1" class="ltx_p">The Kullback–Leibler term admits an equivalent and practically useful interpretation. Using <math id="S1.SS1.p3.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\operatorname{KL}(p\|q)=\sum_{i}p_{i}\log\frac{p_{i}}{q_{i}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>KL</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>∥</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><msub><mo>∑</mo><mi>i</mi></msub><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.167em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mi>log</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mfrac><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><msub><mi>q</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mfrac></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\operatorname{KL}(p\|q)=\sum_{i}p_{i}\log\frac{p_{i}}{q_{i}}</annotation></semantics></math>, we can write</p>
<table id="S1.E3" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S1.E3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\operatorname{KL}\!\big(p_{T}^{(\tau)}\|p_{S}^{(\tau)}\big)=-\sum_{c=1}^{C}p_{T,c}^{(\tau)}(x)\,\log stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo>;</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em">+</mo><mrow><munderover><mo movablelimits="false">∑</mo><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>C</mi></munderover><mrow><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mrow><mi>T</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0.337em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mi>log</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mrow><mi>T</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\operatorname{KL}\!\big(p_{T}^{(\tau)}\|p_{S}^{(\tau)}\big)=-\sum_{c=1}^{C}p_{T,c}^{(\tau)}(x)\,\log p_{S,c}^{(\tau)}(x;w,\theta)+\sum_{c=1}^{C}p_{T,c}^{(\tau)}(x)\,\log p_{T,c}^{(\tau)}(x),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S3)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S1.SS1.p3.3" class="ltx_p">that is,</p>
<table id="S1.E4" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S1.E4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\operatorname{KL}\!\big(p_{T}^{(\tau)}\|p_{S}^{(\tau)}\big)=\operatorname{CE}\!\big(p_{T}^{(\tau)},\,p_{S}^{(\tau)}\big)-\mathrm{H}\!\big(p_{T}^{(\tau)}\big)," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mpadded style="width:1.431em;" width="1.431em"><mi>KL</mi></mpadded><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">(</mo><mrow><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>T</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo>∥</mo><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>S</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup></mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mpadded style="width:1.412em;" width="1.412em"><mi>CE</mi></mpadded><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">(</mo><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>T</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo rspace="0.337em">,</mo><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>S</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mpadded style="width:0.742em;" width="0.742em"><mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">(</mo><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>T</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\operatorname{KL}\!\big(p_{T}^{(\tau)}\|p_{S}^{(\tau)}\big)=\operatorname{CE}\!\big(p_{T}^{(\tau)},\,p_{S}^{(\tau)}\big)-\mathrm{H}\!\big(p_{T}^{(\tau)}\big),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S4)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S1.SS1.p3.2" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S1.SS1.p3.2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathrm{H}(p_{T}^{(\tau)})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msubsup><mi>p</mi><mi>T</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{H}(p_{T}^{(\tau)})</annotation></semantics></math> is the Shannon entropy of the teacher distribution and is independent of the student parameters. Consequently, minimising the KL term is equivalent to minimising cross-entropy against the teacher soft targets<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">hinton2015distilling</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">cover1999elements</span>]</cite>. This encourages the student to reproduce the teacher’s <em id="S1.SS1.p3.2.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">relative class structure</em> (including non-argmax probabilities), which provides a denser training signal than one-hot labels and empirically improves optimisation and generalisation in compressed regimes.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.SS1.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS1.p4.1" class="ltx_p">Finally, in the PQKD setting the distillation signal plays an additional structural role: because the student parameters are restricted to a low-dimensional manifold induced by the photonic-conditioned convolution parameterisation, the teacher soft targets guide the optimisation toward solutions that best approximate the teacher <em id="S1.SS1.p4.1.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">within this constrained model class</em>. In this sense, distillation acts as the mechanism that selects, via <math id="S1.SS1.p4.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(w,\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(w,\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>, a high-performing point on the compression–accuracy frontier reported in the Sec. <a href="#S2.SS2" title="2.2 Training and validation dynamics ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2.2</span></a> and Sec. <a href="#S2.SS3" title="2.3 Scaling compression from partial to full convolutional compression ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2.3</span></a>.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S1.SS2" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S1.2 </span>Model compression and structured parameterisation</h3>

<div id="S1.SS2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS2.p1.1" class="ltx_p">Modern deep networks are frequently over-parameterised relative to the complexity of the target task, yet the resulting parameter budgets can be prohibitive in settings where <em id="S1.SS2.p1.1.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">training-time</em> updates, deployment constraints, or communication overhead dominate<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">zhang2016understanding</span>]</cite>. In particular, for edge inference<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">wang2025low</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">wang2019adaptive</span>]</cite>, federated learning<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">mcmahan2017communication</span>]</cite>, continual learning<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">parisi2019continual</span>]</cite>, and hardware-in-the-loop optimisation<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">wright2022deep</span>]</cite>, the cost of maintaining and updating large weight tensors can exceed the cost of forward computation. Compression methods therefore aim to reduce resource requirements while preserving accuracy, and can be broadly categorised according to the resource being optimised.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.SS2.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS2.p2.1" class="ltx_p">We distinguish three complementary notions of compression:</p>
<ul id="S1.I1" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="S1.I1.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="S1.I1.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.I1.i1.p1.1" class="ltx_p"><span id="S1.I1.i1.p1.1.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Trainable-parameter compression:</span> reducing the number of parameters that must be learned or updated to reach a given performance level. This directly impacts optimisation complexity, storage of trainable state (including optimiser moments), and the communication cost of gradient/parameter synchronisation<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">wang2025parameter</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">zheng2019communication</span>]</cite>.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="S1.I1.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="S1.I1.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.I1.i2.p1.1" class="ltx_p"><span id="S1.I1.i2.p1.1.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Inference compute reduction:</span> reducing the floating-point operations (FLOPs), latency, or energy consumed during inference. This is commonly targeted by pruning, low-rank factorisation, or efficient architectural blocks<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">menghani2023efficient</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">liu2025survey</span>]</cite>.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="S1.I1.i3" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="S1.I1.i3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.I1.i3.p1.1" class="ltx_p"><span id="S1.I1.i3.p1.1.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Bandwidth/memory reduction:</span> reducing the cost of storing, transmitting, or streaming model weights and activations, which can be a dominant bottleneck on modern accelerators due to limited memory bandwidth<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">gholami2024ai</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">kao2023flat</span>]</cite>.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p id="S1.SS2.p2.2" class="ltx_p">These notions are related but not equivalent: for example, a method can sharply reduce trainable parameters while leaving inference FLOPs largely unchanged, or vice versa. In this work, we focus on <em id="S1.SS2.p2.2.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">trainable-parameter compression</em> because PQKD is designed as a structured mechanism that restricts the effective degrees of freedom of convolutional layers while allowing the resulting compressed hypothesis class to be tuned by a compact photonic control signal.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.SS2.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS2.p3.1" class="ltx_p">Our approach follows the principle of <em id="S1.SS2.p3.1.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">structured parameterisation</em>: rather than zeroing or quantising weights post hoc, we explicitly constrain the weight tensors to lie in a low-dimensional family that is efficient to store and update. Convolutional layers are particularly suitable for this strategy because their parameters factor naturally into spatial and channel dimensions. By replacing dense kernels with a dictionary of spatial basis filters and a low-dimensional mixing mechanism (Supplementary Note <a href="#S2a" title="S2 Supplementary Note 2: Definition of Photonic Quantum Knowledge Distillation ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S2</span></a>), PQKD reduces the number of trainable degrees of freedom in the convolutional stack. Knowledge distillation then supplies a dense supervisory signal that mitigates the accuracy loss typically associated with strong constraints, enabling us to trace a controlled compression–accuracy frontier.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S1.SS3" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S1.3 </span>Continuous-variable photonic quantum computing</h3>

<div id="S1.SS3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS3.p1.1" class="ltx_p">Continuous-variable (CV) photonic quantum computing provides a hardware platform in which information is encoded in bosonic modes of the electromagnetic field and processed through optical transformations<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">braunstein2005quantum</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">weedbrook2012gaussian</span>]</cite>. In integrated implementations, the dominant programmable components are reconfigurable interferometric networks composed of beam splitters and phase shifters, optionally augmented by Gaussian operations such as squeezing (when available)<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">wang2020integrated</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">carolan2015universal</span>]</cite>. From a learning-systems perspective, a defining characteristic is that readout is naturally <em id="S1.SS3.p1.1.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">sampling-based</em>: photon-number-resolving (PNR) detection<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">deshpande2022quantum</span>]</cite> or threshold detection<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">quesada2018gaussian</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">hadfield2009single</span>]</cite> produces stochastic outcomes whose empirical statistics converge to an underlying measurement distribution as the shot budget <math id="S1.SS3.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> increases.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.SS3.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS3.p2.2" class="ltx_p">Photonic quantum knowledge distillation (PQKD) is designed to interface directly with this CV photonic sampling model. Rather than requiring analytic gradients through the photonic circuit—which can be challenging under realistic noise, imperfect calibration, or restricted access to device internals—PQKD treats the photonic processor as a controllable stochastic feature generator. Circuit parameters <math id="S1.SS3.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> modulate the output distribution, and a fixed classical feature map converts finite-shot samples into a compact conditioning vector that controls a structured parameterisation of the student network. This separation respects near-term photonic hardware constraints: the photonic device is used in the regime it naturally supports (shot-limited sampling from a programmable optical circuit), while optimisation of the coupled classical–photonic system proceeds with sampling-robust, gradient-free updates for <math id="S1.SS3.p2.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> and standard gradient-based updates for the classical student parameters.</p>
</div>
<div id="S1.SS3.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS3.p3.4" class="ltx_p">A CV photonic circuit can be described as a sequence of elementary gate operations acting on one or more bosonic modes. Each mode is associated with annihilation and creation operators <math id="S1.SS3.p3.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(\hat{a},\hat{a}^{\dagger})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mover accent="true"><mi>a</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>,</mo><msup><mover accent="true"><mi>a</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>†</mo></msup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(\hat{a},\hat{a}^{\dagger})</annotation></semantics></math>, number operator <math id="S1.SS3.p3.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\hat{n}=\hat{a}^{\dagger}\hat{a}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>n</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>=</mo><mrow><msup><mover accent="true"><mi>a</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>†</mo></msup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mover accent="true"><mi>a</mi><mo>^</mo></mover></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\hat{n}=\hat{a}^{\dagger}\hat{a}</annotation></semantics></math>, and quadratures <math id="S1.SS3.p3.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(\hat{x},\hat{p})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mover accent="true"><mi>x</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>,</mo><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(\hat{x},\hat{p})</annotation></semantics></math><cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">braunstein2005quantum</span>]</cite>. In practice, the gate set implemented in integrated photonics is dominated by <em id="S1.SS3.p3.4.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">Gaussian</em> operations—those generated by Hamiltonians at most quadratic in <math id="S1.SS3.p3.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(\hat{a},\hat{a}^{\dagger})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mover accent="true"><mi>a</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>,</mo><msup><mover accent="true"><mi>a</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>†</mo></msup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(\hat{a},\hat{a}^{\dagger})</annotation></semantics></math>—including displacements, rotations, squeezing, and multi-mode linear interferometers built from beam splitters and phase shifters<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">carolan2015universal</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">reck1994experimental</span>]</cite>. Non-Gaussian gates (generated by higher-than-quadratic Hamiltonians), such as Kerr interactions, are more challenging experimentally but are conceptually important because Gaussian operations alone are not universal for quantum computation over CV systems<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">lloyd1999quantum</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">menicucci2006universal</span>]</cite>. In the experiments considered here, the photonic module is parameterised through a programmable interferometer (a product of beam splitters and rotations) and is accessed through sampling-based measurement; therefore, this gate-level description provides a direct bridge between physical programmability and the algorithmic interface<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">quesada2018gaussian</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">deng2023gaussian</span>]</cite>.</p>
</div>
<section id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px1" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Gaussian single- and two-mode gates.</h5>

<div id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.1" class="ltx_p">The elementary Gaussian gates used to construct most CV photonic processors include<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">weedbrook2012gaussian</span>]</cite>:</p>
<ul id="S1.I2" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="S1.I2.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>

<p id="S1.I2.i1.p1.4" class="ltx_p"><span id="S1.I2.i1.p1.4.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Displacement.</span> The displacement gate shifts the phase-space mean of a mode and can be written as</p>

<p id="S1.I2.i2.p1.4" class="ltx_p"><span id="S1.I2.i2.p1.4.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Squeezing.</span> The squeezing gate changes the variances of conjugate quadratures and generates nonclassical states:</p>

<p id="S1.I2.i4.p1.1" class="ltx_p"><span id="S1.I2.i4.p1.1.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Beam splitter.</span> A beam splitter couples two modes through interference:</p>

<p id="S1.I2.i4.p1.2" class="ltx_p">and is the fundamental two-mode primitive used to build general multi-mode linear interferometers.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px2" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">A representative non-Gaussian gate.</h5>

<div id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" class="ltx_p">A canonical example of a non-Gaussian CV gate is the Kerr interaction<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">lloyd1999quantum</span>]</cite>,</p>
<table id="S1.E9" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S1.E9.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\hat{\Phi}(\kappa)=\exp(i\kappa\hat{n}^{2}),\qquad\kappa\in[0,2\pi)," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>κ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>exp</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>κ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mover accent="true"><mi>n</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="2.167em">,</mo><mrow><mi>κ</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mrow><mn>2</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>π</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\hat{\Phi}(\kappa)=\exp(i\kappa\hat{n}^{2}),\qquad\kappa\in[0,2\pi),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S9)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1.2" class="ltx_p">which is generated by a quartic Hamiltonian and can induce highly nonclassical dynamics. While such nonlinearities are generally more demanding to realise in scalable integrated platforms, they are relevant conceptually because adding a suitable non-Gaussian element to Gaussian operations enables universal CV quantum computing. In the present work, we do not rely on explicit Kerr nonlinearities; instead, we exploit sampling-based measurement and classical post-processing as the operational interface to the photonic module.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px3" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Interferometers as products of beam splitters and rotations.</h5>

<div id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1.1" class="ltx_p">A key workhorse in CV photonic hardware is the <math id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>N</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N</annotation></semantics></math>-mode linear interferometer, which implements a unitary transformation on the mode operators. In the lossless case, this transformation can be compiled into a sequence of beam splitters and single-mode rotations (phase shifts). Thus, a programmable interferometer can be represented abstractly as</p>
<table id="S1.E10" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S1.E10.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\hat{U}(\boldsymbol{\vartheta})=\prod_{\ell=1}^{L}\hat{BS}(\theta_{\ell},\phi_{\ell})\prod_{m=1}^{M}\hat{R}(\varphi_{m})," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>U</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi class="ltx_mathvariant_bold-italic" mathvariant="bold-italic">ϑ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><munderover><mo movablelimits="false">∏</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>L</mi></munderover><mrow><mover accent="true"><mrow><mi>B</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow><mo>^</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi></msub><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>ϕ</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><munderover><mo movablelimits="false">∏</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>M</mi></munderover><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>R</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>φ</mi><mi>m</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\hat{U}(\boldsymbol{\vartheta})=\prod_{\ell=1}^{L}\hat{BS}(\theta_{\ell},\phi_{\ell})\prod_{m=1}^{M}\hat{R}(\varphi_{m}),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S10)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1.2" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1.2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\boldsymbol{\vartheta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi class="ltx_mathvariant_bold-italic" mathvariant="bold-italic">ϑ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boldsymbol{\vartheta}</annotation></semantics></math> collects all tunable angles. This is precisely the type of parameterisation that underlies many integrated meshes <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">reck1994experimental</span>, <span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">clements2016optimal</span>]</cite> and loop-based time-bin architectures<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">motes2014scalable</span>]</cite>; in our implementation, this structure manifests as a constraint on the number of beam-splitter parameters per “tiling” (Supplementary Note <a href="#S5" title="S5 Supplementary Note 7: Quantum model details ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S5</span></a>).</p>
</div>
<figure id="S1.T1" class="ltx_table">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_table">Table S1: </span><span id="S1.T1.26.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Common CV gate operations in photonic circuits.</span> Gaussian gates are generated by Hamiltonians at most quadratic in <math id="S1.T1.4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(\hat{a},\hat{a}^{\dagger})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mover accent="true"><mi>a</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>,</mo><msup><mover accent="true"><mi>a</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mo>†</mo></msup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(\hat{a},\hat{a}^{\dagger})</annotation></semantics></math>; Kerr is a representative non-Gaussian gate. In many programmable photonic processors, <math id="S1.T1.5.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\hat{U}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mover accent="true"><mi>U</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\hat{U}</annotation></semantics></math> is implemented as a product of beam splitters and rotations forming an <math id="S1.T1.6.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>N</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N</annotation></semantics></math>-port interferometer.</figcaption>

<div id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p2.1" class="ltx_p">This gate-level view clarifies how PQKD interfaces with CV photonics. The photonic module is parameterised by tunable interferometric angles (implemented physically through phase shifters and couplers) and is queried through repeated measurement. Rather than requiring explicit analytic gradients through the gate sequence, PQKD uses finite-shot samples to construct a stable feature vector <math id="S1.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>, which conditions a structured convolutional parameterisation in the student network. This design aligns the algorithm with the dominant near-term CV photonic capabilities: programmable Gaussian interferometers and sampling-based detection.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
</section>
<section id="S2a" class="ltx_section">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">S2 </span>Supplementary Note 2: Definition of Photonic Quantum Knowledge Distillation</h2>

<section id="S2.SS1a" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S2.1 </span>Photonic quantum feature map</h3>

<div id="S2.SS1a.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1a.p1.1" class="ltx_p">The role of the photonic module in PQKD is to provide a compact, hardware-aligned <em id="S2.SS1a.p1.1.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">conditioning signal</em> for the compressed student network<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">cimini2024variational</span>]</cite>. Operationally, the photonic processor is accessed through repeated measurement: for a fixed input preparation and a programmable optical circuit, we observe finite-shot samples from an output distribution whose statistics depend on a low-dimensional parameter vector <math id="S2.SS1a.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math><cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">cerezo2021variational</span>]</cite>. PQKD converts these samples into a deterministic, fixed-length feature vector that can be used by standard deep-learning components without requiring an analytic differentiable model of the photonic device.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS1a.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1a.p2.3" class="ltx_p">Formally, let <math id="S2.SS1a.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\rho_{\mathrm{in}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rho_{\mathrm{in}}</annotation></semantics></math> denote a fixed <math id="S2.SS1a.p2.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>N</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N</annotation></semantics></math>-mode input state and let <math id="S2.SS1a.p2.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="U(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>U</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">U(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> be a parameterised CV unitary representing the programmable photonic transformation. The output state is</p>
<table id="S2.E11a" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E11a.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\rho_{\theta}=U(\theta)\,\rho_{\mathrm{in}}\,U(\theta)^{\dagger}." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>U</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>U</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>†</mo></msup></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rho_{\theta}=U(\theta)\,\rho_{\mathrm{in}}\,U(\theta)^{\dagger}.</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S11)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1a.p2.5" class="ltx_p">A measurement described by a positive operator-valued measure (POVM) <math id="S2.SS1a.p2.4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\{E_{\omega}\}_{\omega\in\Omega}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><msub><mi>E</mi><mi>ω</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mrow><mi>ω</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">Ω</mi></mrow></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{E_{\omega}\}_{\omega\in\Omega}</annotation></semantics></math> induces a probability distribution over outcomes <math id="S2.SS1a.p2.5.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\omega\in\Omega" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>ω</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">Ω</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\omega\in\Omega</annotation></semantics></math>,</p>
<table id="S2.E12a" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E12a.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{\theta}(\omega)=\operatorname{Tr}\!\big(E_{\omega}\rho_{\theta}\big)," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ω</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mpadded style="width:1.032em;" width="1.032em"><mi>Tr</mi></mpadded><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>E</mi><mi>ω</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub></mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">p_{\theta}(\omega)=\operatorname{Tr}\!\big(E_{\omega}\rho_{\theta}\big),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S12)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1a.p2.8" class="ltx_p">which captures all device-level effects relevant to the algorithmic interface. In practice, the distribution is not accessed directly; instead, we obtain <math id="S2.SS1a.p2.6.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> independent shots <math id="S2.SS1a.p2.7.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\omega_{1},\ldots,\omega_{S}\sim p_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>ω</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>ω</mi><mi>S</mi></msub></mrow><mo>∼</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\omega_{1},\ldots,\omega_{S}\sim p_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math> and construct an empirical distribution (histogram) <math id="S2.SS1a.p2.8.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{p}_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{p}_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math>. The photonic quantum feature map is then defined as</p>
<table id="S2.E13a" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E13a.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)=\Phi(\widehat{p}_{\theta})\in\mathbb{R}^{d}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mi>d</mi></msup></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)=\Phi(\widehat{p}_{\theta})\in\mathbb{R}^{d},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S13)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS1a.p2.9" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S2.SS1a.p2.9.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Phi" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Phi</annotation></semantics></math> is a fixed classical post-processing rule that (i) aggregates shot-limited outcomes into a stable representation, (ii) produces a constant-dimensional vector compatible with neural-network layers, and (iii) is inexpensive relative to the downstream classical training.</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS1a.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1a.p3.4" class="ltx_p">This design makes explicit that the photonic contribution enters PQKD through <em id="S2.SS1a.p3.4.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">distributional statistics</em> rather than single-shot values: <math id="S2.SS1a.p3.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> summarises the circuit-dependent measurement behaviour and serves as a low-dimensional control signal for structured parameter generation in the student network (Supplementary Note <a href="#S2a" title="S2 Supplementary Note 2: Definition of Photonic Quantum Knowledge Distillation ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S2</span></a>). The shot budget <math id="S2.SS1a.p3.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> sets the statistical fidelity of <math id="S2.SS1a.p3.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{p}_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{p}_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math> and therefore governs the variance of <math id="S2.SS1a.p3.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>; this dependence motivates the noise and stability analyses reported in Sec. <a href="#S2.SS4" title="2.4 Robustness to shot noise and hardware-relevant perturbations ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2.4</span></a> and the use of variance-reduction strategies such as feature smoothing (Supplementary Note <a href="#S6" title="S6 Supplementary Note 8: Training protocol ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S6</span></a>).</p>
</div>
<div id="S2.SS1a.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS1a.p4.3" class="ltx_p">In the main experiments, we use <math id="S2.SS1a.p4.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N=16" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>16</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N=16</annotation></semantics></math> modes and construct a <math id="S2.SS1a.p4.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d=512" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>512</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">d=512</annotation></semantics></math> dimensional feature vector by concatenating two <math id="S2.SS1a.p4.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="256" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>256</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">256</annotation></semantics></math>-bin marginal histograms derived from 8-bit partitions of thresholded detection outcomes (Supplementary Note <a href="#S5" title="S5 Supplementary Note 7: Quantum model details ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S5</span></a>). This choice balances representational richness with robustness under finite shots, and yields a fixed interface that remains unchanged across compression configurations (compressing one, two, or all convolutional layers).</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S2.SS2a" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S2.2 </span>Photonic-conditioned dictionary convolution</h3>

<div id="S2.SS2a.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS2a.p1.1" class="ltx_p">PQKD compresses convolutional layers by replacing a fully trainable kernel tensor with a <em id="S2.SS2a.p1.1.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">structured, low-dimensional parameterisation</em> whose effective degrees of freedom are controlled by the photonic feature vector <math id="S2.SS2a.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>. This section provides a complete mathematical specification of the parameterisation, its implementation-friendly tensor shapes, and its trainable-parameter accounting.</p>
</div>
<section id="S2.SS2.SSS0.Px1" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Standard convolution.</h5>

<div id="S2.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S2.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.4" class="ltx_p">Consider an input activation map <math id="S2.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{in}}\times H\times W}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>H</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>W</mi></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">x\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{in}}\times H\times W}</annotation></semantics></math> and an output activation map <math id="S2.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="h\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}\times H^{\prime}\times W^{\prime}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><msup><mi>H</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><msup><mi>W</mi><mo>′</mo></msup></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">h\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}\times H^{\prime}\times W^{\prime}}</annotation></semantics></math>. A standard 2D convolution layer with kernel size <math id="S2.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="k\times k" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k\times k</annotation></semantics></math> and padding <math id="S2.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{\mathrm{pad}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>pad</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">p_{\mathrm{pad}}</annotation></semantics></math> is parameterised by a weight tensor</p>
<table id="S2.E14a" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S2.E14a.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="W\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}\times C_{\mathrm{in}}\times k\times k}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>W</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>k</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></msup></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">W\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}\times C_{\mathrm{in}}\times k\times k},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S14)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S2.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.5" class="ltx_p">and optional bias <math id="S2.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>out</mi></msub></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">b\in\mathbb{R}^{C_{\mathrm{out}}}</annotation></semantics></math>. The output is</p>
