<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S63)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1.4" class="ltx_p">Here <math id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1.3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="[\theta;\mathbf{0}]" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo>;</mo><mn>𝟎</mn><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">[\theta;\mathbf{0}]</annotation></semantics></math> denotes concatenation with zeros. This adjustment guarantees that every call to the photonic sampler receives a valid parameter vector, while allowing us to treat <math id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px3.p1.4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo rspace="0em">dim</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dim(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> as a controlled hyperparameter in compression sweeps.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px4" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Implementation details and practical considerations.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.1" class="ltx_p">For numerical stability and physical interpretability of the underlying interferometric angles, we additionally apply a fixed bounding operation to <math id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta_{\mathrm{fit}}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi>fit</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta_{\mathrm{fit}}</annotation></semantics></math> when required by the backend (e.g., wrapping angles to a principal interval):</p>
<table id="S5.E64" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S5.E64.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta_{\mathrm{fit}}\leftarrow\mathrm{wrap}(\theta_{\mathrm{fit}};[-\pi,\pi])\quad\text{or}\quad\theta_{\mathrm{fit}}\leftarrow\mathrm{clip}(\theta_{\mathrm{fit}};[-\theta_{\max},\theta_{\max}])," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi>fit</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">←</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>wrap</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi>fit</mi></msub><mo>;</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mrow><mo>−</mo><mi>π</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mi>π</mi><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mspace style="width:1em;" width="1em"></mspace><mtext>or</mtext></mrow></mrow><mspace style="width:1em;" width="1em"></mspace><mrow><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi>fit</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">←</mo><mrow><mi>clip</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi>fit</mi></msub><mo>;</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mrow><mo>−</mo><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi>max</mi></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi>max</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta_{\mathrm{fit}}\leftarrow\mathrm{wrap}(\theta_{\mathrm{fit}};[-\pi,\pi])\quad\text{or}\quad\theta_{\mathrm{fit}}\leftarrow\mathrm{clip}(\theta_{\mathrm{fit}};[-\theta_{\max},\theta_{\max}]),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S64)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.3" class="ltx_p">where the specific convention is held constant across all runs. Importantly, the tiling expansion in Eq. (<a href="#S5.E59" title="In Tiling interpretation for extended parameter vectors. ‣ S5.1 Circuit family and theta-length constraint ‣ S5 Supplementary Note 7: Quantum model details ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S59</span></a>) increases the effective circuit depth (number of repeated mixing stages) without changing the mode count <math id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>N</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N</annotation></semantics></math>, and therefore provides a principled way to scale the photonic control capacity while maintaining a fixed feature dimension <math id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p1.3.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>d</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">d</annotation></semantics></math> and a fixed sampling interface.</p>
</div>
<div id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p2.1" class="ltx_p">Overall, this theta-length constraint is not merely a software artefact: it reflects a physically motivated parameterisation of a structured interferometric circuit family. Our deterministic mapping in Eq. (<a href="#S5.E63" title="In Deterministic adjustment for sampler compatibility. ‣ S5.1 Circuit family and theta-length constraint ‣ S5 Supplementary Note 7: Quantum model details ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S63</span></a>) ensures strict sampler compatibility, reproducible hyperparameter sweeps over <math id="S5.SS1.SSS0.Px4.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo rspace="0em">dim</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dim(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>, and a clear interpretation of additional photonic parameters as additional interferometric tiles.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS2" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S5.2 </span>Measurement and sample format</h3>

<div id="S5.SS2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS2.p1.1" class="ltx_p">PQKD accesses the photonic processor through repeated measurements. Each circuit execution (shot) produces a multi-mode detection outcome whose statistics depend on the circuit parameters <math id="S5.SS2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> and the chosen input state preparation. To make the downstream feature construction well-defined and hardware-aligned, we adopt a standard <em id="S5.SS2.p1.1.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">thresholded</em> measurement representation that converts raw detection events into a fixed-length binary vector over modes.</p>
</div>
<section id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Measurement model.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.5" class="ltx_p">Let <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\rho_{\theta}=U(\theta)\rho_{\mathrm{in}}U(\theta)^{\dagger}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>U</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>in</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>U</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>†</mo></msup></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rho_{\theta}=U(\theta)\rho_{\mathrm{in}}U(\theta)^{\dagger}</annotation></semantics></math> be the output state of the <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>N</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N</annotation></semantics></math>-mode photonic circuit. A single shot applies a measurement described by a POVM <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\{E_{\omega}\}_{\omega\in\Omega}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><msub><mi>E</mi><mi>ω</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mrow><mi>ω</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">Ω</mi></mrow></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{E_{\omega}\}_{\omega\in\Omega}</annotation></semantics></math> and returns a random outcome <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\omega\sim p_{\theta}(\omega)=\operatorname{Tr}(E_{\omega}\rho_{\theta})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>ω</mi><mo>∼</mo><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ω</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>Tr</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>E</mi><mi>ω</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>ρ</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\omega\sim p_{\theta}(\omega)=\operatorname{Tr}(E_{\omega}\rho_{\theta})</annotation></semantics></math>. In photon-counting settings<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">hadfield2009single</span>]</cite>, <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\omega" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>ω</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\omega</annotation></semantics></math> can be represented as a photon-number pattern</p>
<table id="S5.E65" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S5.E65.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n=(n_{1},\ldots,n_{N})\in\mathbb{Z}_{\geq 0}^{N}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>N</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msubsup><mi>ℤ</mi><mrow><mi></mi><mo>≥</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><mi>N</mi></msubsup></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">n=(n_{1},\ldots,n_{N})\in\mathbb{Z}_{\geq 0}^{N},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S65)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.7" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.6.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n_{j}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">n_{j}</annotation></semantics></math> is the number of detected photons in mode <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px1.p1.7.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="j" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>j</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">j</annotation></semantics></math>. In threshold-detection settings, the detector reports only whether each mode is “clicked” (occupied) or “not clicked” (empty)<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">quesada2018gaussian</span>]</cite>, which can be viewed as a coarse-graining of photon-number measurements.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Thresholding to a binary occupancy vector.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" class="ltx_p">For consistency across backends and to reduce sensitivity to rare high-count events, we convert each raw pattern <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>n</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">n</annotation></semantics></math> into a binary occupancy vector</p>
<table id="S5.E66" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S5.E66.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b=(b_{1},\ldots,b_{N})\in\{0,1\}^{N},\qquad b_{j}=\mathbb{I}[\,n_{j}&gt;0\,]," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>b</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>b</mi><mi>N</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mi>N</mi></msup></mrow><mo rspace="2.167em">,</mo><mrow><msub><mi>b</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>𝕀</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo rspace="0.170em" stretchy="false">[</mo><mrow><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><mo lspace="0.170em" stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">b=(b_{1},\ldots,b_{N})\in\{0,1\}^{N},\qquad b_{j}=\mathbb{I}[\,n_{j}&gt;0\,],</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S66)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2.p1.7" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2.p1.2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{I}[\cdot]" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>𝕀</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">⋅</mo><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbb{I}[\cdot]</annotation></semantics></math> is the indicator function. Thus, each shot yields a length-<math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2.p1.3.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>N</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N</annotation></semantics></math> bitstring <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2.p1.4.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>b</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">b</annotation></semantics></math> encoding per-mode occupancy. We denote the resulting random variable by <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2.p1.5.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="B\sim P_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>B</mi><mo>∼</mo><msub><mi>P</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">B\sim P_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math> over <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2.p1.6.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\{0,1\}^{N}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mi>N</mi></msup><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{0,1\}^{N}</annotation></semantics></math>, where <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px2.p1.7.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="P_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>P</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">P_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math> is the induced distribution after thresholding.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px3" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Finite-shot sampling and empirical distribution.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px3.p1.1" class="ltx_p">For a single feature evaluation, we collect <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px3.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> independent samples</p>
<table id="S5.E67" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S5.E67.m1" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="b^{(1)},\ldots,b^{(S)}\ \overset{\mathrm{i.i.d.}}{\sim}\ P_{\theta}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mrow><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>S</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mover accent="true"><mo>∼</mo><mrow><mi mathsize="0.700em" mathvariant="normal">i</mi><mo lspace="0em" mathsize="0.700em" rspace="0.167em">.</mo><mi mathsize="0.700em" mathvariant="normal">i</mi><mo lspace="0em" mathsize="0.700em" rspace="0.167em">.</mo><mi mathsize="0.700em" mathvariant="normal">d</mi><mo lspace="0em" mathsize="0.700em">.</mo></mrow></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>P</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">b^{(1)},\ldots,b^{(S)}\ \overset{\mathrm{i.i.d.}}{\sim}\ P_{\theta},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S67)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px3.p1.4" class="ltx_p">and compute empirical statistics (e.g., histograms of selected marginals) to form <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px3.p1.2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{p}_{\theta}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{p}_{\theta}</annotation></semantics></math> and the corresponding feature vector <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px3.p1.3.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)=\Phi(\widehat{p}_{\theta})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>p</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)=\Phi(\widehat{p}_{\theta})</annotation></semantics></math> (Supplementary Note <a href="#S2.SS1a" title="S2.1 Photonic quantum feature map ‣ S2 Supplementary Note 2: Definition of Photonic Quantum Knowledge Distillation ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S2.1</span></a>). In all experiments, <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px3.p1.4.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> is treated as an explicit hyperparameter controlling the trade-off between feature variance and evaluation cost, and the impact of finite-shot noise is studied in Supplementary Note <a href="#S3.SS3" title="S3.3 Finite-shot noise propagation ‣ S3 Supplementary Note 3: Theory—expressivity, approximation, and stability ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S3.3</span></a> and Supplementary Note <a href="#S2.SS4" title="2.4 Robustness to shot noise and hardware-relevant perturbations ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2.4</span></a>.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px4" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Implementation.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px4.p1.2" class="ltx_p">In code, the sampler returns either an array of per-shot samples of shape <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px4.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(S,N)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>S</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>N</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(S,N)</annotation></semantics></math> with entries in <math id="S5.SS2.SSS0.Px4.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\{0,1\}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{0,1\}</annotation></semantics></math> (after thresholding), or an equivalent representation (e.g., integer-encoded bitstrings) that can be deterministically converted to the binary format in Eq. (<a href="#S5.E66" title="In Thresholding to a binary occupancy vector. ‣ S5.2 Measurement and sample format ‣ S5 Supplementary Note 7: Quantum model details ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S66</span></a>). We standardise all outputs to the binary matrix representation to ensure that feature construction and parameter generation are backend-agnostic.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS3" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S5.3 </span>Feature construction</h3>

<div id="S5.SS3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS3.p1.1" class="ltx_p">This subsection specifies the exact photonic feature map <math id="S5.SS3.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Phi" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Phi</annotation></semantics></math> used in the main experiments. The guiding design goal is to transform shot-limited binary detection patterns into a <em id="S5.SS3.p1.1.1" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">fixed-length</em>, <em id="S5.SS3.p1.1.2" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">order-consistent</em>, and <em id="S5.SS3.p1.1.3" class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">variance-controlled</em> representation that (i) is simple to implement, (ii) remains stable under finite-shot sampling, and (iii) preserves meaningful distributional information beyond per-mode means.</p>
</div>
<section id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px1" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Bitstring partitioning.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.2" class="ltx_p">Each shot produces a thresholded occupancy vector <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b\in\{0,1\}^{N}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mi>N</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">b\in\{0,1\}^{N}</annotation></semantics></math> with <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N=16" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>16</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N=16</annotation></semantics></math> modes (Supplementary Note <a href="#S5.SS2" title="S5.2 Measurement and sample format ‣ S5 Supplementary Note 7: Quantum model details ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S5.2</span></a>). We partition the bitstring into two contiguous 8-bit halves,</p>
<table id="S5.E68" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S5.E68.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b=\big[b^{(1)};\,b^{(2)}\big],\qquad b^{(1)}\in\{0,1\}^{8},\ \ b^{(2)}\in\{0,1\}^{8}." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">[</mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo rspace="0.337em">;</mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>2</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">]</mo></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="2.167em">,</mo><mrow><mrow><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mn>8</mn></msup></mrow><mo rspace="1.167em">,</mo><mrow><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>2</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mn>8</mn></msup></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">b=\big[b^{(1)};\,b^{(2)}\big],\qquad b^{(1)}\in\{0,1\}^{8},\ \ b^{(2)}\in\{0,1\}^{8}.</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S68)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.4" class="ltx_p">This produces two low-dimensional views (marginals) of the <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="16" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>16</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">16</annotation></semantics></math>-bit outcome. Importantly, this construction avoids the exponential <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(2^{16})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msup><mn>2</mn><mn>16</mn></msup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(2^{16})</annotation></semantics></math> histogram that would be too sparse under realistic shot budgets, while still capturing structured multi-bit correlations within each half.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px2" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Index mapping.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" class="ltx_p">For each half <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b^{(m)}=(b^{(m)}_{1},\ldots,b^{(m)}_{8})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msubsup><mi>b</mi><mn>1</mn><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msubsup><mi>b</mi><mn>8</mn><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">b^{(m)}=(b^{(m)}_{1},\ldots,b^{(m)}_{8})</annotation></semantics></math>, we define a deterministic integer encoding</p>
<table id="S5.E69" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S5.E69.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathrm{idx}\!\left(b^{(m)}\right)=\sum_{j=1}^{8}b^{(m)}_{j}\,2^{8-j}\in\{0,1,\ldots,255\},\qquad m\in\{1,2\}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><mpadded style="width:1.267em;" width="1.267em"><mi>idx</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><munderover><mo movablelimits="false">∑</mo><mrow><mi>j</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mn>8</mn></munderover><mrow><msubsup><mi>b</mi><mi>j</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msup><mn> 2</mn><mrow><mn>8</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>j</mi></mrow></msup></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mn>255</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="2.167em">,</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>2</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{idx}\!\left(b^{(m)}\right)=\sum_{j=1}^{8}b^{(m)}_{j}\,2^{8-j}\in\{0,1,\ldots,255\},\qquad m\in\{1,2\},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S69)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1.2" class="ltx_p">where the bit ordering convention (most-significant to least-significant) is fixed throughout all runs. Any consistent convention is valid as long as it is held constant across training and evaluation.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px3" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Empirical marginal histograms.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1.3" class="ltx_p">Given <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> i.i.d. samples <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\{b_{s}\}_{s=1}^{S}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msubsup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><msub><mi>b</mi><mi>s</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>S</mi></msubsup><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{b_{s}\}_{s=1}^{S}</annotation></semantics></math>, we compute the two empirical marginal histograms <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="h^{(1)},h^{(2)}\in\mathbb{R}^{256}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msup><mi>h</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo>,</mo><msup><mi>h</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>2</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mn>256</mn></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">h^{(1)},h^{(2)}\in\mathbb{R}^{256}</annotation></semantics></math>:</p>
<table id="S5.E70" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S5.E70.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="h^{(m)}[k]=\frac{1}{S}\sum_{s=1}^{S}\mathbf{1}\Big\{\mathrm{idx}\!\left(b^{(m)}_{s}\right)=k\Big\},\qquad k\in\{0,\ldots,255\},\ \ m\in\{1,2\}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><msup><mi>h</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>k</mi><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mi>S</mi></mfrac><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><munderover><mo movablelimits="false">∑</mo><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>S</mi></munderover><mrow><mn>𝟏</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.600em" minsize="1.600em">{</mo><mrow><mrow><mpadded style="width:1.267em;" width="1.267em"><mi>idx</mi></mpadded><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo>(</mo><msubsup><mi>b</mi><mi>s</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup><mo>)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow><mo maxsize="1.600em" minsize="1.600em">}</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="2.167em">,</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mn>255</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="1.167em">,</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>2</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">h^{(m)}[k]=\frac{1}{S}\sum_{s=1}^{S}\mathbf{1}\Big\{\mathrm{idx}\!\left(b^{(m)}_{s}\right)=k\Big\},\qquad k\in\{0,\ldots,255\},\ \ m\in\{1,2\},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S70)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1.4" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px3.p1.4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbf{1}\{\cdot\}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mn>𝟏</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">⋅</mo><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{1}\{\cdot\}</annotation></semantics></math> is the indicator function. By construction, each histogram is a valid empirical probability mass function:</p>
<table id="S5.E71" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">

</div>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Concatenation and standardisation.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1.1" class="ltx_p">We form a <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="512" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>512</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">512</annotation></semantics></math>-dimensional feature by concatenating the two marginals:</p>
<table id="S5.E72" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S5.E72.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tilde{z}(\theta)=\big[h^{(1)};\,h^{(2)}\big]\in\mathbb{R}^{512}." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>~</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">[</mo><msup><mi>h</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo rspace="0.337em">;</mo><msup><mi>h</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>2</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">]</mo></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mn>512</mn></msup></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\tilde{z}(\theta)=\big[h^{(1)};\,h^{(2)}\big]\in\mathbb{R}^{512}.</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S72)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1.8" class="ltx_p">To improve numerical conditioning and to make the scale of the conditioning signal comparable across runs, we apply an affine standardisation:</p>
<table id="S5.E73" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S5.E73.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)=\gamma\cdot\frac{\tilde{z}(\theta)-\mu}{\sigma+\epsilon}\in\mathbb{R}^{512}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>γ</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mfrac><mrow><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>~</mo></mover><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mi>μ</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>ϵ</mi></mrow></mfrac></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mn>512</mn></msup></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)=\gamma\cdot\frac{\tilde{z}(\theta)-\mu}{\sigma+\epsilon}\in\mathbb{R}^{512},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S73)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1.7" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1.2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mu\in\mathbb{R}^{512}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mn>512</mn></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mu\in\mathbb{R}^{512}</annotation></semantics></math> and <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1.3.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma\in\mathbb{R}^{512}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>ℝ</mi><mn>512</mn></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\sigma\in\mathbb{R}^{512}</annotation></semantics></math> are fixed reference statistics and <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1.4.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\epsilon&gt;0" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>ϵ</mi><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\epsilon&gt;0</annotation></semantics></math> is a small stabiliser (added elementwise) to avoid division by zero. In our implementation, <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1.5.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(\mu,\sigma)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>μ</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>σ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(\mu,\sigma)</annotation></semantics></math> are computed once from an initial set of feature evaluations (e.g., using a fixed seed and the initial <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1.6.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math>) and then held fixed for the remainder of training; this ensures that the mapping <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px4.p1.7.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Phi" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi mathvariant="normal">Φ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Phi</annotation></semantics></math> remains deterministic and does not leak label information.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px5" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Interpretation and trade-offs.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px5.p1.4" class="ltx_p">The two-marginal design in Eq. (<a href="#S5.E70" title="In Empirical marginal histograms. ‣ S5.3 Feature construction ‣ S5 Supplementary Note 7: Quantum model details ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S70</span></a>)–(<a href="#S5.E73" title="In Concatenation and standardisation. ‣ S5.3 Feature construction ‣ S5 Supplementary Note 7: Quantum model details ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S73</span></a>) offers a practical compromise between expressivity and sample efficiency. A full histogram over <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px5.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\{0,1\}^{16}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mn>16</mn></msup><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{0,1\}^{16}</annotation></semantics></math> would require <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px5.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="2^{16}=65{,}536" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>2</mn><mn>16</mn></msup><mo>=</mo><mrow><mn>65</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>536</mn></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2^{16}=65{,}536</annotation></semantics></math> bins and would be extremely sparse for typical shot budgets. In contrast, the two 8-bit marginals use only <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px5.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="2\times 256=512" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mn>256</mn></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>512</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2\times 256=512</annotation></semantics></math> bins, yielding more reliable estimates under finite shots while preserving higher-order correlations within each half. The finite-shot concentration behaviour follows the scaling in Supplementary Note <a href="#S3.SS3" title="S3.3 Finite-shot noise propagation ‣ S3 Supplementary Note 3: Theory—expressivity, approximation, and stability ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S3.3</span></a> with effective histogram size <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px5.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="K=512" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>K</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>512</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">K=512</annotation></semantics></math>.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px6" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Implementation note.</h5>

<div id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px6.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px6.p1.5" class="ltx_p">In code, if samples are returned as a binary matrix <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px6.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="B\in\{0,1\}^{S\times 16}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>B</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mn>16</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">B\in\{0,1\}^{S\times 16}</annotation></semantics></math>, the index mapping in Eq. (<a href="#S5.E69" title="In Index mapping. ‣ S5.3 Feature construction ‣ S5 Supplementary Note 7: Quantum model details ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S69</span></a>) can be computed by a dot product with a fixed weight vector <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px6.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(2^{7},2^{6},\ldots,2^{0})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msup><mn>2</mn><mn>7</mn></msup><mo>,</mo><msup><mn>2</mn><mn>6</mn></msup><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msup><mn>2</mn><mn>0</mn></msup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(2^{7},2^{6},\ldots,2^{0})</annotation></semantics></math>. Histograms are then obtained by counting occurrences over <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px6.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="k\in\{0,\ldots,255\}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mn>255</mn><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k\in\{0,\ldots,255\}</annotation></semantics></math> and normalising by <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px6.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math>. The final <math id="S5.SS3.SSS0.Px6.p1.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> is produced by concatenation and elementwise standardisation as in Eq. (<a href="#S5.E73" title="In Concatenation and standardisation. ‣ S5.3 Feature construction ‣ S5 Supplementary Note 7: Quantum model details ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S73</span></a>).</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
</section>
<section id="S6" class="ltx_section">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">S6 </span>Supplementary Note 8: Training protocol</h2>

<div id="S6.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.p1.1" class="ltx_p">This Supplementary Note describes the full training procedure used for PQKD, including teacher optimisation, student optimisation under knowledge distillation, and the update rule for photonic parameters. The protocol is designed to be reproducible and to reflect the operational constraints of a shot-based photonic backend: the photonic module is accessed through repeated sampling to construct features, while the classical student is trained using standard gradient-based optimisation. Because the photonic feature affects the student through a non-analytic sampling interface, we adopt an alternating optimisation strategy that approximates a bilevel objective.</p>
</div>
<section id="S6.SS1" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S6.1 </span>Data splits, preprocessing, and evaluation</h3>

<div id="S6.SS1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS1.p1.1" class="ltx_p">Unless otherwise stated, we use a fixed train/validation/test split and fixed random seeds for dataset subsampling and mini-batch ordering. Inputs are standardised according to dataset conventions (e.g., per-channel normalisation for CIFAR-10) and augmented only when explicitly indicated. All reported validation and test metrics are computed deterministically (no dropout, fixed batch ordering, no data augmentation at evaluation time). Accuracy is reported as top-1 classification accuracy; cross-entropy refers to the standard negative log-likelihood loss.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S6.SS2" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S6.2 </span>Teacher training</h3>

<div id="S6.SS2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS2.p1.3" class="ltx_p">Teachers are trained with hard-label cross-entropy using Adam with default learning rate <math id="S6.SS2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="10^{-3}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msup><mn>10</mn><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>3</mn></mrow></msup><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">10^{-3}</annotation></semantics></math> for 100 epochs unless otherwise stated. We use batch size 64 and apply standard regularisation consistent with the teacher architecture (e.g., dropout in <span id="S6.SS2.p1.3.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter">conv3</span>). Let teacher logits be <math id="S6.SS2.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="t(x)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>t</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">t(x)</annotation></semantics></math> and hard labels be <math id="S6.SS2.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>y</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">y</annotation></semantics></math>. The teacher objective is</p>
<table id="S6.E74" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S6.E74.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\min_{\psi}\ \mathbb{E}_{(x,y)\sim\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{train}}}\Big[\operatorname{CE}\big(y,\operatorname{softmax}(t(x;\psi))\big)\Big]," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><munder><mi>min</mi><mi>ψ</mi></munder><mo lspace="0.667em">⁡</mo><msub><mi>𝔼</mi><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>y</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>∼</mo><msub><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">𝒟</mi><mi>train</mi></msub></mrow></msub></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.600em" minsize="1.600em">[</mo><mrow><mi>CE</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">(</mo><mi>y</mi><mo>,</mo><mrow><mi>softmax</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>t</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo>;</mo><mi>ψ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo maxsize="1.600em" minsize="1.600em">]</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\min_{\psi}\ \mathbb{E}_{(x,y)\sim\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{train}}}\Big[\operatorname{CE}\big(y,\operatorname{softmax}(t(x;\psi))\big)\Big],</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S74)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S6.SS2.p1.4" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S6.SS2.p1.4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\psi" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>ψ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\psi</annotation></semantics></math> denotes teacher parameters. The best-performing checkpoint is selected using validation accuracy and then evaluated once on the held-out test set.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S6.SS3" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S6.3 </span>Alternating optimisation for PQKD</h3>

<section id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px1" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Bilevel viewpoint.</h5>

<div id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.3" class="ltx_p">PQKD introduces two coupled sets of learnable variables: classical student weights <math id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> and photonic circuit parameters <math id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math>. The student weights are optimised to minimise a training distillation loss, while <math id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> is optimised to improve generalisation as measured by a validation proxy objective computed using the photonic feature map. This structure can be expressed as the bilevel problem</p>
<table id="S6.E75" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S6.E75.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w^{\ast}(\theta)\in\arg\min_{w}\ \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{train}}_{\mathrm{KD}}(w,\theta),\qquad\theta^{\ast}\in\arg\min_{\theta}\ \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{val}}_{\mathrm{KD}}\!\big(w^{\ast}(\theta),\theta\big)." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><msup><mi>w</mi><mo>∗</mo></msup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>arg</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mrow><munder><mi>min</mi><mi>w</mi></munder><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><msubsup><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">ℒ</mi><mi>KD</mi><mi>train</mi></msubsup></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="2.167em">,</mo><mrow><msup><mi>θ</mi><mo>∗</mo></msup><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>arg</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mrow><munder><mi>min</mi><mi>θ</mi></munder><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><msubsup><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">ℒ</mi><mi>KD</mi><mi>val</mi></msubsup></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">(</mo><mrow><msup><mi>w</mi><mo>∗</mo></msup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w^{\ast}(\theta)\in\arg\min_{w}\ \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{train}}_{\mathrm{KD}}(w,\theta),\qquad\theta^{\ast}\in\arg\min_{\theta}\ \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{val}}_{\mathrm{KD}}\!\big(w^{\ast}(\theta),\theta\big).</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S75)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.4" class="ltx_p">Direct bilevel optimisation is typically computationally expensive, especially when the outer variable <math id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> only influences the model through shot-based samples. We therefore employ an alternating scheme that approximates Eq. (<a href="#S6.E75" title="In Bilevel viewpoint. ‣ S6.3 Alternating optimisation for PQKD ‣ S6 Supplementary Note 8: Training protocol ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S75</span></a>) with a small number of outer updates per epoch.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px2" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Operational training loop.</h5>

<div id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" class="ltx_p">Each student epoch consists of two phases:</p>
<ol id="S6.I1" class="ltx_enumerate">
<li id="S6.I1.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">1.</span> 
<div id="S6.I1.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.I1.i1.p1.4" class="ltx_p"><span id="S6.I1.i1.p1.4.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Photonic phase (outer updates):</span> perform <math id="S6.I1.i1.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\texttt{theta\_updates\_per\_epoch}=10" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mtext class="ltx_mathvariant_monospace">theta_updates_per_epoch</mtext><mo>=</mo><mn>10</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\texttt{theta\_updates\_per\_epoch}=10</annotation></semantics></math> SPSA steps to update <math id="S6.I1.i1.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> while holding <math id="S6.I1.i1.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> fixed. Each SPSA step uses a validation mini-batch (or a small fixed set of validation batches) to evaluate the proxy objective <math id="S6.I1.i1.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">J(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="S6.I1.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">2.</span> 
<div id="S6.I1.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.I1.i2.p1.2" class="ltx_p"><span id="S6.I1.i2.p1.2.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Classical phase (inner updates):</span> perform one epoch of Adam updates on <math id="S6.I1.i2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> using the distillation loss, holding <math id="S6.I1.i2.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math> fixed (equivalently, holding the photonic feature used by the student fixed for that epoch).</p>
</div>
</li>
</ol>
<p id="S6.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1.2" class="ltx_p">This schedule yields a practical and stable separation of concerns: classical optimisation proceeds with smooth gradients on training data, while photonic optimisation is driven by a generalisation-oriented signal from validation performance and uses only function evaluations through the sampling backend.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section id="S6.SS4" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S6.4 </span>SPSA photonic updates</h3>

<section id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px1" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Validation proxy objective.</h5>

<div id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px1.p1.5" class="ltx_p">Let <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px1.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">J(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> denote the scalar objective used for outer-loop updates. In our implementation, <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px1.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">J(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> is defined as the negative validation accuracy (or, equivalently, the validation distillation loss) computed with the current student weights <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px1.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> and with the photonic feature map evaluated at <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px1.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\theta" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>θ</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\theta</annotation></semantics></math>. Because the feature is shot-limited, <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px1.p1.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">J(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> is stochastic; we reduce variance by averaging over a small number of validation mini-batches.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">SPSA estimator.</h5>

<div id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.2" class="ltx_p">Simultaneous Perturbation Stochastic Approximation (SPSA) provides an efficient gradient-free update that requires only two objective evaluations per step, independent of <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo rspace="0em">dim</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\dim(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math><cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<span class="ltx_ref ltx_missing_citation ltx_ref_self">spall2002multivariate</span>]</cite>. At SPSA step <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="k" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>k</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math>, we draw a Rademacher perturbation vector</p>
<table id="S6.E76" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S6.E76.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\Delta_{k}\in\{\pm 1\}^{\dim(\theta)}\qquad\text{with i.i.d.\ entries}." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi>k</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><mrow><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mrow><mo>±</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0em">dim</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></msup><mspace style="width:2em;" width="2em"></mspace><mtext>with i.i.d. entries</mtext></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\Delta_{k}\in\{\pm 1\}^{\dim(\theta)}\qquad\text{with i.i.d.\ entries}.</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S76)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.6" class="ltx_p">We then evaluate the objective at symmetric perturbations</p>
<table id="S6.E77" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>

<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S77)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.7" class="ltx_p">and form the stochastic gradient estimate</p>
<table id="S6.E78" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S6.E78.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{g}_{k}=\frac{J(\theta_{k}^{+})-J(\theta_{k}^{-})}{2c}\,\Delta_{k}." display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>g</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>k</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mfrac><mrow><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msubsup><mi>θ</mi><mi>k</mi><mo>+</mo></msubsup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msubsup><mi>θ</mi><mi>k</mi><mo>−</mo></msubsup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mfrac><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></mrow><mo lspace="0em">.</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{g}_{k}=\frac{J(\theta_{k}^{+})-J(\theta_{k}^{-})}{2c}\,\Delta_{k}.</annotation></semantics></math></td>

</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.8" class="ltx_p">The parameter update is</p>
<table id="S6.E79" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>

</table>
<p id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.4" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a&gt;0" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">a&gt;0</annotation></semantics></math> is the step size and <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c&gt;0" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">c&gt;0</annotation></semantics></math> is the perturbation scale. For stability and to respect backend parameter constraints, we apply elementwise clipping</p>
<table id="S6.E80" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
