<p id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.5" class="ltx_p">In all experiments, <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(a,c,\theta_{\max})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>c</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>θ</mi><mi>max</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(a,c,\theta_{\max})</annotation></semantics></math> are held fixed within a sweep and reported alongside the corresponding results.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px3" class="ltx_paragraph">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph">Relation to finite-shot noise.</h5>

<div id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px3.p1.4" class="ltx_p">Because <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px3.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">J(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> depends on shot-limited features (Supplementary Note <a href="#S3.SS3" title="S3.3 Finite-shot noise propagation ‣ S3 Supplementary Note 3: Theory—expressivity, approximation, and stability ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S3.3</span></a>), <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px3.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\widehat{g}_{k}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>g</mi><mo>^</mo></mover><mi>k</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\widehat{g}_{k}</annotation></semantics></math> is a noisy estimate. The use of symmetric perturbations in Eq. (<a href="#S6.E78" title="In SPSA estimator. ‣ S6.4 SPSA photonic updates ‣ S6 Supplementary Note 8: Training protocol ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S78</span></a>) cancels some common-mode sampling noise, and evaluating <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px3.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">J(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> on multiple validation mini-batches further reduces variance. We report noise impact studies by varying the shot budget <math id="S6.SS4.SSS0.Px3.p1.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>S</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S</annotation></semantics></math> and observing its effect on stability and final accuracy (Supplementary Note <a href="#S6.SS6" title="S6.6 EMA feature smoothing ‣ S6 Supplementary Note 8: Training protocol ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S6.6</span></a>).</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section id="S6.SS5" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S6.5 </span>Classical student updates</h3>

<div id="S6.SS5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS5.p1.3" class="ltx_p">During the classical phase, student weights <math id="S6.SS5.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="w" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>w</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">w</annotation></semantics></math> are optimised using Adam on the training distillation objective. Let <math id="S6.SS5.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="s(x;w,\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo>;</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">s(x;w,\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> denote student logits given the current photonic feature (fixed for the epoch). The update minimises <math id="S6.SS5.p1.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{train}}_{\mathrm{KD}}(w,\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msubsup><mi class="ltx_font_mathcaligraphic">ℒ</mi><mi>KD</mi><mi>train</mi></msubsup><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>w</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{train}}_{\mathrm{KD}}(w,\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> defined in Eq. (<a href="#S1.E2" title="In S1.1 Knowledge distillation ‣ S1 Supplementary Note 1: Fundamentals ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S2</span></a>). We use the same batch size (64) as the teacher unless otherwise stated. Training is performed with standard best practices: gradients are backpropagated only through the classical student network; no gradients are propagated through the photonic sampler, consistent with our black-box sampling interface.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="S6.SS6" class="ltx_subsection">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">S6.6 </span>EMA feature smoothing</h3>

<div id="S6.SS6.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS6.p1.2" class="ltx_p">Finite-shot photonic sampling produces a stochastic estimate of the conditioning feature <math id="S6.SS6.p1.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> used to parameterise the compressed student. If injected directly, this sampling noise appears as high-frequency, epoch-to-epoch innovations in the feature stream and can be amplified by the student’s sensitivity to <math id="S6.SS6.p1.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>z</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z</annotation></semantics></math>, degrading optimisation stability at fixed shot budgets (Supplementary Note <a href="#S3.SS3" title="S3.3 Finite-shot noise propagation ‣ S3 Supplementary Note 3: Theory—expressivity, approximation, and stability ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">S3.3</span></a>). To suppress these fluctuations without modifying the photonic circuit or measurement procedure, we optionally apply exponential moving average (EMA) smoothing to the feature sequence:</p>
<table id="S6.E81" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S6.E81.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\bar{z}_{t}\;=\;\beta\,\bar{z}_{t-1}+(1-\beta)\,z_{t}(\theta),\qquad\beta\in[0,1)," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover><mi>t</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.558em" rspace="0.558em">=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>β</mi><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover><mrow><mi>t</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msub></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><msub><mi>z</mi><mi>t</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="2.167em">,</mo><mrow><mi>β</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bar{z}_{t}\;=\;\beta\,\bar{z}_{t-1}+(1-\beta)\,z_{t}(\theta),\qquad\beta\in[0,1),</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S81)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S6.SS6.p1.6" class="ltx_p">where <math id="S6.SS6.p1.3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="t" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mi>t</mi><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">t</annotation></semantics></math> indexes feature evaluations (epochs in our implementation) and <math id="S6.SS6.p1.4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\bar{z}_{0}=z_{0}(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover><mn>0</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>z</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bar{z}_{0}=z_{0}(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>. When enabled, the student forward pass uses <math id="S6.SS6.p1.5.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\bar{z}_{t}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover><mi>t</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bar{z}_{t}</annotation></semantics></math> in place of the instantaneous sample <math id="S6.SS6.p1.6.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z_{t}(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>z</mi><mi>t</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z_{t}(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>.</p>
</div>
<div id="S6.SS6.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS6.p2.4" class="ltx_p">EMA acts as a causal low-pass filter: it preserves slowly varying components of the photonic signal while attenuating rapid innovations that are predominantly induced by finite-shot fluctuations. A useful interpretation follows from the decomposition <math id="S6.SS6.p2.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z_{t}(\theta)=\mu(\theta)+\varepsilon_{t}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>z</mi><mi>t</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>ε</mi><mi>t</mi></msub></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z_{t}(\theta)=\mu(\theta)+\varepsilon_{t}</annotation></semantics></math> with <math id="S6.SS6.p2.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{E}[\varepsilon_{t}]=0" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>𝔼</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><msub><mi>ε</mi><mi>t</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbb{E}[\varepsilon_{t}]=0</annotation></semantics></math> and approximately independent increments <math id="S6.SS6.p2.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\varepsilon_{t}" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><msub><mi>ε</mi><mi>t</mi></msub><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\varepsilon_{t}</annotation></semantics></math> across successive evaluations. Under this standard approximation, <math id="S6.SS6.p2.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{E}[\bar{z}_{t}]=\mu(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi>𝔼</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover><mi>t</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbb{E}[\bar{z}_{t}]=\mu(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> (no bias in the mean signal), and the variance of the smoothed estimate is reduced relative to the raw estimate by</p>
<table id="S6.E82" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S6.E82.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\frac{\mathrm{Var}(\bar{z}_{t})}{\mathrm{Var}(z_{t})}\;\approx\;\frac{1-\beta}{1+\beta}," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mfrac><mrow><mi>Var</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover><mi>t</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mrow><mi>Var</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>z</mi><mi>t</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mfrac><mo lspace="0.558em" rspace="0.558em">≈</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>+</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow></mfrac></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{\mathrm{Var}(\bar{z}_{t})}{\mathrm{Var}(z_{t})}\;\approx\;\frac{1-\beta}{1+\beta},</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S82)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S6.SS6.p2.5" class="ltx_p">with the reduction becoming sharper as <math id="S6.SS6.p2.5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\beta\rightarrow 1" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>β</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\beta\rightarrow 1</annotation></semantics></math>. Equivalently, EMA yields an effective increase in sampling budget,</p>
<table id="S6.E83" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_left"><math id="S6.E83.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S_{\mathrm{eff}}\;\approx\;\frac{1+\beta}{1-\beta}\,S," display="block" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>S</mi><mi>eff</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.558em" rspace="0.558em">≈</mo><mrow><mfrac><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>+</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow></mfrac><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S_{\mathrm{eff}}\;\approx\;\frac{1+\beta}{1-\beta}\,S,</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_left_padright"></td>
<td rowspan="1" class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_eqno ltx_align_middle ltx_align_right"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_equation ltx_align_right">(S83)</span></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p id="S6.SS6.p2.6" class="ltx_p">so that the student experiences a feature stream comparable to one obtained with substantially more shots, but at the same physical measurement cost per epoch.</p>
</div>
<div id="S6.SS6.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p id="S6.SS6.p3.8" class="ltx_p">In our MNIST EMA-mechanism trace at <math id="S6.SS6.p3.1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S{=}200" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>200</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S{=}200</annotation></semantics></math> shots and <math id="S6.SS6.p3.2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\beta{=}0.9" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mi>β</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0.9</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\beta{=}0.9</annotation></semantics></math>, the distribution of per-dimension variance ratios <math id="S6.SS6.p3.3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathrm{Var}(z_{\mathrm{used}})/\mathrm{Var}(z_{\mathrm{raw}})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>Var</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>z</mi><mi>used</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>/</mo><mi>Var</mi></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>z</mi><mi>raw</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{Var}(z_{\mathrm{used}})/\mathrm{Var}(z_{\mathrm{raw}})</annotation></semantics></math> concentrates well below unity, with a median <math id="S6.SS6.p3.4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="0.0406" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>0.0406</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.0406</annotation></semantics></math> (IQR <math id="S6.SS6.p3.5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="0.0322" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>0.0322</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.0322</annotation></semantics></math>–<math id="S6.SS6.p3.6.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="0.0532" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>0.0532</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.0532</annotation></semantics></math>) over the analysis window, consistent with the theoretical attenuation level <math id="S6.SS6.p3.7.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(1-\beta)/(1+\beta)=0.0526" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>+</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0.0526</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(1-\beta)/(1+\beta)=0.0526</annotation></semantics></math> and the corresponding amplification <math id="S6.SS6.p3.8.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S_{\mathrm{eff}}\approx 19\,S" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>S</mi><mi>eff</mi></msub><mo>≈</mo><mrow><mn>19</mn><mo lspace="0.170em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S_{\mathrm{eff}}\approx 19\,S</annotation></semantics></math>. These observations support the role of EMA as a simple, hardware-compatible variance-reduction mechanism for stabilising PQKD in shot-limited regimes, and complement the robustness results in Sec. <a href="#S2.SS4" title="2.4 Robustness to shot noise and hardware-relevant perturbations ‣ 2 Results ‣ Photonic Quantum-Enhanced Knowledge Distillation" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2.4</span></a>.</p>
</div>

<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure S1: </span><span id="S6.F1.9.1" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">EMA suppresses shot-noise fluctuations in the photonic conditioning signal.</span>

<span id="S6.F1.11.3" class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">(b)</span> Windowed value distributions across feature dimensions for the raw and EMA-used signals; the dashed curve indicates the removed residual <math id="S6.F1.3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(z_{\mathrm{raw}}-z_{\mathrm{EMA}})" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>z</mi><mi>raw</mi></msub><mo>−</mo><msub><mi>z</mi><mi>EMA</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(z_{\mathrm{raw}}-z_{\mathrm{EMA}})</annotation></semantics></math>.

</figure>
</section>

<div id="alg1.l11" class="ltx_listingline">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_listingline"><span id="alg1.l11.1.1.1" class="ltx_text" style="font-size:80%;">11:</span></span>   <math id="alg1.l11.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\bar{z}\leftarrow\beta\bar{z}+(1-\beta)z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover><mo stretchy="false">←</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>β</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>β</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bar{z}\leftarrow\beta\bar{z}+(1-\beta)z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math>   (initialise <math id="alg1.l11.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\bar{z}=z(\theta)" display="inline" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><mi>z</mi><mo>¯</mo></mover><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bar{z}=z(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math> if empty)
